  ---
  SECTION IV: DYNAMIC COOPERATION CLUSTERING (DCC)

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  Remember the pizza delivery analogy from Section III? Every driver was
  delivering to every customer вҖ” that was the scalability disaster.

  Dynamic Cooperation Clustering (DCC) is the solution framework. The idea is
  elegantly simple:

  Each customer is served only by the few nearest drivers. Each driver only
  serves the few nearest customers.

  Imagine you live in a large city. You order pizza. Instead of every driver in
  the city preparing your order, only the 2-3 drivers nearest to your house are
  assigned to you. Similarly, each driver is only responsible for the 5-10
  customers nearest to them.

  The key word is "dynamic" вҖ” the assignments change based on:
  - Where customers are located (if you move, different drivers serve you)
  - Channel conditions (if a building blocks the signal from one AP, another AP
  takes over)
  - Network load (busy APs hand off users to less busy neighbors)

  The "clusters" overlap. Your house might be served by Drivers A, B, and C.
  Your neighbor might be served by Drivers B, C, and D. Driver B and C serve
  both of you вҖ” the clusters overlap. There are no rigid boundaries like in
  traditional cells.

  The magic is a simple on/off switch: for each AP-UE pair, there's a switch
  that says "AP l serves UE i" (switch ON) or "AP l does NOT serve UE i" (switch
   OFF). These switches are captured mathematically by diagonal matrices DбөўвӮ—.

  This section shows that:
  1. The original Cell-Free Massive MIMO (where every switch is ON) is just one
  extreme case
  2. Traditional cellular networks (where only one AP per UE is ON) is another
  extreme
  3. DCC encompasses everything in between
  4. If you limit how many "ON switches" each AP has, you get scalability

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 The DCC Framework вҖ” Origin and Core Idea

  The DCC framework was proposed by BjГ¶rnson, JaldГ©n, Bengtsson, and Ottersten
  (2011) [17] to enable:

  в–Һ "unified analysis of anything from interference channels to Network MIMO"

  The genius of the framework is that it captures ALL possible cooperation
  strategies using a single mathematical object: a set of diagonal selection 
  matrices.

  Definition: For each UE i = 1,...,K and each AP l = 1,...,L, define a diagonal
   matrix:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— вҲҲ в„ӮбҙәЛЈбҙә     (N Г— N diagonal matrix)

  The j-th diagonal element of DбөўвӮ— is:

  в–Һ [DбөўвӮ—]вұјвұј = { 1  if the j-th antenna of AP l is allowed to transmit to / 
  decode from UE i
  в–Һ              { 0  otherwise

  Physical meaning: DбөўвӮ— is a binary switch matrix that controls which antennas
  at AP l participate in serving UE i.

  2.2 Special Cases of DбөўвӮ—

  Case 1: Full service вҖ” AP l serves UE i with all N antennas:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ     (N Г— N identity matrix вҖ” all antennas ON)

  Case 2: No service вҖ” AP l does not serve UE i at all:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ     (N Г— N zero matrix вҖ” all antennas OFF)

  Case 3: Partial service вҖ” Only some antennas of AP l serve UE i:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = diag(1, 0, 1, 0)     (example for N = 4: antennas 1 and 3 are ON)

  In practice, the paper mostly uses Case 1 or Case 2 (full AP-level selection),
   leading to the simplified Eq. (11). Per-antenna selection is theoretically
  possible but rarely used.

  2.3 The Block-Diagonal Aggregate Matrix DвӮ–

  For UE k, stack all L matrices into a block-diagonal aggregate:

  в–Һ DвӮ– = diag(DвӮ–вӮҒ, DвӮ–вӮӮ, ..., DвӮ–вӮ—) вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙ№ЛЈбҙ№

  This M Г— M block-diagonal matrix acts as a network-wide mask that selects
  which of the M = NL total antennas participate in serving UE k.

  2.4 Two Key Set Definitions

  Set в„ібөў вҖ” the set of APs serving UE i:

  в–Һ в„ібөў вҠӮ {1, ..., L}     where l вҲҲ в„ібөў  вҹә  DбөўвӮ— вү  0вӮҷ

  This is the "AP cluster for UE i" вҖ” the user-centric cluster shown in Fig. 2
  of the paper.

  Set рқ’ҹвӮ— вҖ” the set of UEs served by AP l (Equation 12):

  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮ— = { i : tr(DбөўвӮ—) вүҘ 1, i вҲҲ {1, ..., K} }          ... (Eq. 12)

  This is the "UE set of AP l" вҖ” the set of UEs that AP l needs to allocate
  resources to.

  These two sets are duals of each other: в„ібөў tells you "which APs serve UE i"
  (UE's perspective), while рқ’ҹвӮ— tells you "which UEs does AP l serve" (AP's
  perspective).

  2.5 Section IV-A: UL and DL Data Transmission with DCC

  The DCC framework modifies the signal models from Section III by inserting the
   selection matrices.

  2.5.1 UL Signal Model with DCC (Equation 9)

  The physical received signal at AP l does not change вҖ” all APs still
  physically receive signals from all UEs:

  в–Һ yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + nвӮ—          (same as Eq. 5)

  However, the DCC framework changes which APs participate in decoding. Only APs
   in в„івӮ– process UE k's signal. The estimate of sвӮ– becomes:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ          ... (Eq. 9, first line)

  Using the collective vectors:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n     ... (Eq. 9)

  Compare with the original Eq. (6):

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ Original (Eq. 6) в”Ӯ    DCC (Eq. 9)    в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Desired signal в”Ӯ vвӮ–бҙҙ hвӮ– sвӮ–        в”Ӯ vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– sвӮ–      в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Interference   в”Ӯ вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ hбөў sбөў   в”Ӯ вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў sбөў в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Noise          в”Ӯ vвӮ–бҙҙ n            в”Ӯ vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n          в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The insertion of DвӮ– is the only difference. It zeroes out the contributions
  from APs not serving UE k.

  Key insight about the UL: Even though AP l physically receives signals from
  ALL UEs, when DвӮ–вӮ— = 0вӮҷ, the contribution vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = 0вӮҷбөҖ yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = 0. So AP l
   simply does not participate in decoding UE k.

  2.5.2 DL Signal Model with DCC (Equation 10)

  The received DL signal at UE k becomes:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў + nвӮ–          ... (Eq. 10)

  Using collective vectors:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ–          ... (Eq. 10, compact)

  Key mechanism: When DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ, then DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ вҖ” AP l does not transmit to UE
   i. Only APs with l вҲҲ в„ібөў (i.e., DбөўвӮ— вү  0вӮҷ) actually transmit the signal
  intended for UE i.

  Similarly for UL combining: vбөўвӮ—бҙҙ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷбөҖ when DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ, so only APs in в„ібөў
  apply receive combining for UE i.

  2.6 DCC Unifies Multiple Architectures

  The beauty of DCC is that it captures many different network architectures by
  choosing {DвӮҒ, ..., DвӮ–} differently:

  Architecture 1: Original Cell-Free Massive MIMO

  в–Һ Dбөў = IвӮҳ   вҲҖ i          (i.e., DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ вҲҖ i, l)

  Every AP serves every UE with all antennas. Eq. (9) reduces to Eq. (6) and Eq.
   (10) reduces to Eq. (7).

  Architecture 2: User-Centric Cell-Free Massive MIMO [27]

  Let в„ібөў вҠӮ {1, ..., L} be the subset of APs serving UE i. Then:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = { IвӮҷ   if l вҲҲ в„ібөў              ... (Eq. 11)
  в–Һ          { 0вӮҷ   if l вҲү в„ібөў

  This is exactly the setup considered in [17] (the original DCC paper) and
  later in [27] (Buzzi & D'Andrea's user-centric Cell-Free approach).

  Architecture 3: Fog Massive MIMO [29]

  Bursalioglu et al. (2019) proposed the "Fog Massive MIMO" architecture for
  DL-only transmission. It uses рқ’ңбөў instead of в„ібөў to denote the AP subset, but is
   otherwise identical to Eq. (11) вҖ” a direct instance of DCC.

  Architecture 4: Traditional Cellular Network (not in paper, but implied)

  Each UE is served by exactly one AP (the "home" base station):

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = { IвӮҷ   if l = l*(i)     (one specific AP)
  в–Һ          { 0вӮҷ   otherwise

  This gives |в„ібөў| = 1 for all i вҖ” each UE has a cluster of size 1 (its cell).

  Architecture 5: Network-Centric Clustering (disjoint, like 4G CoMP)

  APs are partitioned into non-overlapping groups {рқ’һвӮҒ, ..., рқ’һвӮҳ}:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = { IвӮҷ   if l вҲҲ рқ’һвӮҳ and UE i is in cluster m's coverage
  в–Һ          { 0вӮҷ   otherwise

  The clusters are disjoint: рқ’һвӮҳ вҲ© рқ’һвӮҳ' = вҲ… for m вү  m'. This creates hard cluster
  boundaries with inter-cluster interference.

  Unified view:

  Interference        Cellular          Disjoint           User-Centric
  Full Cell-Free
  Channel            (1 AP/UE)         CoMP Clusters       DCC/CF-mMIMO
  (All APs/All UEs)
    вҶҗв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  в”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’
   DбөўвӮ— mostly 0     DбөўвӮ—=IвӮҷ for 1 AP   DбөўвӮ—=IвӮҷ in cluster  DбөўвӮ—=IвӮҷ for nearby
  Dбөў=IвӮҳ вҲҖi
   No cooperation     Minimal coop.      Moderate coop.      Smart coop.
    Full coop.
                                                             (SCALABLE)
    (UNSCALABLE)

  2.7 Section IV-B: A Partial Solution to the Scalability Issue

  Now comes the critical scalability result.

  Lemma 1

  в–Һ If the cardinality |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ for l = 1, ..., L, then the 
  Cell-Free Massive MIMO network with DCC satisfies the first three conditions 
  in Definition 1.

  Proof (from the paper):

  If |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ, then:

  Criterion 1 (Channel estimation): AP l only needs to compute channel estimates
   for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs (not all K UEs). Complexity = |рқ’ҹвӮ—| В· NВІ = O(1) as K вҶ’ вҲһ. вң“

  Criterion 2 (Signal processing): AP l only computes combining/precoding
  vectors for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs:
  - UL: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| inner products, each N multiplications вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮ—| В· N = O(1) вң“
  - DL: sum of |рқ’ҹвӮ—| precoded signals вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮ—| В· N = O(1) вң“

  Criterion 3 (Fronthaul): AP l only sends/receives data for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs вҶ’ O(1)
  scalars per time slot вң“

  What about Criterion 4 (Power control)? Lemma 1 does NOT cover this. Power
  control scalability must be achieved separately вҖ” for example, by using
  heuristic algorithms like equal power allocation or the fractional allocation
  in Eq. (43).

  The practical question: How do we choose the sets рқ’ҹвӮ— in a scalable way while
  guaranteeing that every UE is served by at least one AP? This is addressed in
  Section V.

  в”Ӯ 2016 в”Ӯ 4G CoMP deployed     в”Ӯ cell-edge improvement),       в”Ӯ [14]      в”Ӯ

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ 2017 в”Ӯ Buzzi & D'Andrea     в”Ӯ User-centric Cell-Free        в”Ӯ [27]      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ Massive MIMO (a DCC instance) в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ 2019 в”Ӯ Bursalioglu et al.   в”Ӯ Fog Massive MIMO (a DCC       в”Ӯ [29]      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ instance for DL)              в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ Proves CF-mMIMO is a DCC      в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ 2020 в”Ӯ This paper           в”Ӯ special case; achieves        в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ provable scalability          в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  3.2 The 4G CoMP Failure вҖ” Lessons Learned

  4G LTE-Advanced (3GPP Release 11) introduced Coordinated Multi-Point (CoMP)
  with three modes:

  1. Joint Transmission (JT): Multiple cells transmit the same data to a
  cell-edge UE
  2. Dynamic Point Selection (DPS): Only one cell transmits at a time, but the
  cell can change dynamically
  3. Coordinated Scheduling/Beamforming (CS/CB): Cells coordinate scheduling but
   don't share data

  In DCC notation:
  - JT: DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ for all l in the cooperation cluster
  - DPS: DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ for exactly one l, switching over time
  - CS/CB: No data sharing; only scheduling coordination (not captured by DCC's
  data-sharing model)

  Why CoMP failed to deliver:
  1. Disjoint clustering: APs divided into fixed, non-overlapping groups вҶ’
  cell-edge problem shifted to cluster boundaries
  2. Backhaul latency: Sharing CSI and data over backhaul was too slow for
  real-time cooperation
  3. FDD operation: DL CSI feedback was inaccurate and expensive (overhead
  proportional to number of antennas)
  4. Intra-site only: In practice, only sectors of the same physical site
  cooperated (2-3 antennas), not across sites

  The lesson that led to Cell-Free Massive MIMO: Use TDD (no CSI feedback), use
  UL pilots (overhead independent of antennas), use user-centric overlapping
  clusters (no cluster boundaries), use distributed processing (no centralized
  backhaul bottleneck).

  Source: A. Osseiran, J. F. Monserrat, and P. Marsch, 5G Mobile and Wireless 
  Communications Technology, Cambridge University Press, 2016, Ch. 9.

  3.3 The Original DCC Paper вҖ” BjГ¶rnson et al. (2011)

  The seminal DCC paper [17] was titled:

  в–Һ "Optimality Properties, Distributed Strategies, and Measurement-Based 
  Evaluation of Coordinated Multicell OFDMA Transmission"

  Published in IEEE Trans. Signal Process., vol. 59, no. 12, pp. 6086вҖ“6101, Dec.
   2011.

  Key contributions:
  - Introduced the inner circle / outer circle cooperation model: each UE has a
  personalized set of BSs that either jointly transmit data (inner circle) or
  suppress interference (outer circle)
  - Proved optimality properties of the cooperation framework
  - Proposed distributed strategies that converge to the optimal solution
  - Validated with real-world measurements

  The DCC framework was later formalized and extended in the textbook:

  в–Һ E. BjГ¶rnson and E. Jorswieck, "Optimal Resource Allocation in Coordinated 
  Multi-Cell Systems," Foundations and Trends in Communications and Information 
  Theory, vol. 9, no. 2-3, pp. 113вҖ“381, 2013. [10]

  This textbook provided [10, Sec. 1] examples showing DCC encompasses
  interference channels, cognitive radio, cellular, CoMP, and Network MIMO вҖ” a
  true unified framework.

  3.4 User-Centric Approaches in the Cell-Free Literature

  Three key papers reintroduced user-centric ideas in the Cell-Free context, but
   with important limitations:

  Buzzi & D'Andrea (2017) [27]:
  - Each UE is served by the nearest П„вӮҡ APs
  - Problem: Does not guarantee all UEs are served (some UEs could be "orphaned"
   if too many nearby UEs compete for the same APs)
  - Is a DCC instance with Eq. (11)

  Ngo, Tran, Duong, Matthaiou, Larsson (2018) [28]:
  - Studied total energy efficiency
  - Problem: Does not limit how many UEs each AP serves вҶ’ unscalable

  Bursalioglu, Caire, Mungara, Papadopoulos, Wang (2019) [29]:
  - "Fog Massive MIMO" вҖ” a user-centric, seamless hot-spot architecture
  - DL only
  - Also a DCC instance

  What was missing in ALL three: Connection to DCC, mathematical proof of
  scalability, handling of initial access, pilot assignment, and channel
  estimation in a unified scalable framework. This paper provides all of these.

  ---
  4. MATHEMATICAL DEEP DIVE

  4.1 The DбөўвӮ— Matrix вҖ” Formal Definition

  DбөўвӮ— вҲҲ в„ӮбҙәЛЈбҙә is a diagonal matrix. For AP-level selection (Eq. 11), it takes one
   of two values:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ  (l вҲҲ в„ібөў)     or     DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ  (l вҲү в„ібөў)

  Properties:
  - DбөўвӮ— is idempotent: DбөўвӮ—ВІ = DбөўвӮ— (since diagonal entries are 0 or 1)
  - DбөўвӮ— is Hermitian: DбөўвӮ—бҙҙ = DбөўвӮ— (real diagonal entries)
  - DбөўвӮ— is a projection matrix: it projects vectors onto the subspace of
  "active" antennas

  Action on vectors:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— hбөўвӮ— = { hбөўвӮ—  if l вҲҲ в„ібөў     (channel preserved)
  в–Һ                  { 0вӮҷ   if l вҲү в„ібөў     (channel zeroed out)

  4.2 Derivation of UL Equation (9) вҖ” Step by Step

  Starting from the received signal at AP l (Eq. 5):

  в–Һ yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + nвӮ—

  AP l applies combining vвӮ–вӮ—, but gated by DвӮ–вӮ—:

  в–Һ vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + nвӮ—)

  If DвӮ–вӮ— = 0вӮҷ: the result is zero вҖ” AP l is silent for UE k.
  If DвӮ–вӮ— = IвӮҷ: the result is vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ вҖ” AP l fully participates.

  Summing over all APs:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ

  Expanding:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— nвӮ—

  в–Һ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— hбөўвӮ— sбөў + вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— nвӮ—

  Rearranging (swap sums, separate desired and interference):

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = (вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— hвӮ–вӮ—) sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· (вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— hбөўвӮ—) sбөў + вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё 
  vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— nвӮ—

  Using collective notation with DвӮ– = diag(DвӮ–вӮҒ, ..., DвӮ–вӮ—):

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n          ... (Eq. 9) вң“

  4.3 Derivation of DL Equation (10) вҖ” Step by Step

  Each AP l transmits a signal intended for all UEs it serves:

  в–Һ xвӮ—бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў

  Note: when DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ, the term DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ вҖ” AP l does not transmit to UE i.
  The transmitted signal only includes UEs in рқ’ҹвӮ—.

  UE k receives:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ xвӮ—бөҲЛЎ + nвӮ–

  в–Һ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў + nвӮ–

  Using collective notation:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ–          ... (Eq. 10) вң“

  Crucial difference from original Eq. (7): The Dбөў matrix multiplies wбөў, zeroing
   out the precoding at APs that don't serve UE i. Each AP only needs to compute
   and transmit precoding for the UEs in its set рқ’ҹвӮ—.

  4.4 Proving the Original Cell-Free is a DCC Special Case

  Set Dбөў = IвӮҳ for all i = 1, ..., K. Then:

  UL (Eq. 9):
  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ n
  в–Һ = vвӮ–бҙҙ hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ n = Eq. (6) вң“

  DL (Eq. 10):
  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· IвӮҳ wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ– = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ– = Eq. (7) вң“

  4.5 Proof of Lemma 1 вҖ” Detailed

  Lemma 1: If |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ for l = 1, ..., L, then the first three
  scalability conditions are satisfied.

  Proof:

  Criterion 1 вҖ” Channel estimation: AP l only estimates channels for UEs in рқ’ҹ

в—Ҹ Now I have all the context. Here is the comprehensive Section IV explanation.

  ---
  SECTION IV: DYNAMIC COOPERATION CLUSTERING (DCC)

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  Let's return to our pizza delivery analogy. In Section III, we saw the
  problem: every driver delivers to every customer вҖ” unscalable.

  Dynamic Cooperation Clustering (DCC) is the solution framework. The idea:

  Each customer is assigned a small team of nearby drivers. Customer A might be
  served by drivers {1, 3, 5}. Customer B might be served by drivers {3, 4, 6}.
  Notice that driver 3 serves both customers вҖ” the teams overlap. This
  overlapping is the key feature.

  Why "dynamic"? Because the teams change over time. If a customer moves to a
  new area, their team is updated to the nearest drivers.

  Why "clustering"? Because each customer has a "cluster" of drivers assigned to
   them.

  The magic: Each driver only serves a small, fixed number of customers (say, at
   most 10). Whether the total number of customers is 100 or 100,000, each
  driver's workload stays the same. This is scalability.

  Section IV does three things:
  1. Introduces the mathematical tool (DбөўвӮ— matrices) that controls which APs
  serve which UEs
  2. Shows that the original Cell-Free Massive MIMO and several other
  architectures are all special cases of this one framework
  3. Proves that DCC partially solves the scalability problem (the first 3 of 4
  criteria)

  Think of DCC as a universal "control panel" with one switch per AP-UE pair.
  Flip a switch ON вҶ’ that AP serves that UE. Flip it OFF вҶ’ it doesn't. Different
   switch configurations create different network architectures:
  - All switches ON вҶ’ Original Cell-Free Massive MIMO
  - Each switch ON only for nearby pairs вҶ’ User-centric Cell-Free (scalable!)
  - Switches ON in disjoint groups вҶ’ Traditional cellular with cooperation
  clusters (4G CoMP)

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 The DCC Framework вҖ” Core Mathematical Tool

  The DCC framework was originally proposed by BjГ¶rnson, JaldГ©n, Bengtsson, and
  Ottersten (2011) [17] and further formalized in the textbook [10] by BjГ¶rnson
  and Jorswieck (2013). Its purpose: provide a "unified analysis of anything
  from interference channels to Network MIMO."

  The core tool is a set of diagonal selection matrices:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— вҲҲ в„ӮбҙәЛЈбҙә ,    for i = 1, ..., K  and  l = 1, ..., L

  These are diagonal matrices that determine which antennas at AP l may transmit
   to (and decode signals from) UE i.

  Structure of DбөўвӮ—: Since it is diagonal, it has the form:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = diag(dВ№бөўвӮ—, dВІбөўвӮ—, ..., dбҙәбөўвӮ—)

  where dКІбөўвӮ— вҲҲ {0, 1} is a binary indicator:
  - dКІбөўвӮ— = 1 вҶ’ the j-th antenna of AP l is allowed to transmit to/decode UE i
  - dКІбөўвӮ— = 0 вҶ’ the j-th antenna of AP l is not involved with UE i

  Key insight: By choosing the KГ—L matrices {DбөўвӮ—} appropriately, we can model
  virtually any multi-AP network architecture within one unified framework.

  2.2 The Block-Diagonal Aggregate Matrix

  For UE k, define the collective selection matrix by stacking:

  в–Һ DвӮ– = diag(DвӮ–вӮҒ, DвӮ–вӮӮ, ..., DвӮ–вӮ—) вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙ№ЛЈбҙ№

  This is an MГ—M block-diagonal matrix (M = NL). When this multiplies the
  collective combining vector vвӮ– вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙ№, it zeroes out the components
  corresponding to APs that are not serving UE k.

  2.3 Section IV-A: UL Data Transmission with DCC (Equation 9)

  The DCC framework does not change the received UL signal yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ in Eq. (5) вҖ” all
   APs still physically receive signals from all UEs (radio waves don't obey
  cluster boundaries). What changes is the processing: only a subset of APs
  participate in decoding each UE.

  The estimate of sвӮ– under DCC becomes:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ        ... (Eq. 9, first line)

  Using collective notation:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– В· sвӮ–  +  вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў В· sбөў  +  vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n        ... 
  (Eq. 9)

  Comparing with Eq. (6) from Section III: The only difference is the insertion
  of DвӮ–. This matrix acts as a filter вҖ” it sets to zero the contributions from
  APs that are not in UE k's cooperation cluster.

  Effect of DвӮ–вӮ— = 0вӮҷ: If AP l does not serve UE k, then DвӮ–вӮ— = 0вӮҷ, which means:
  - DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = 0 вҶ’ AP l contributes nothing to ЕқвӮ–
  - vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— = 0бөҖ вҶ’ the combining vector for that AP doesn't matter (it's zeroed
   out)

  Effect of DвӮ–вӮ— = IвӮҷ: If AP l fully serves UE k, then DвӮ–вӮ— = IвӮҷ, and AP l
  participates normally вҖ” exactly as in the original Cell-Free model.

  2.4 Section IV-A: DL Data Transmission with DCC (Equation 10)

  The received DL signal at UE k under DCC:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў  +  nвӮ–        ... (Eq. 10, expanded)

  In collective notation:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў  +  nвӮ–        ... (Eq. 10, compact)

  Key difference from Eq. (7): The precoding vector wбөўвӮ— is multiplied by DбөўвӮ—
  before transmission. When DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ вҶ’ AP l transmits nothing for UE i

  So only APs with DбөўвӮ— вү  0вӮҷ actually transmit to UE i. This is how DCC limits
  each AP's DL workload.

  2.5 How Different Network Architectures Are Special Cases of DCC

  This is one of the most elegant results in the section. The paper shows that
  several previously proposed architectures are ALL special cases:

  Case 1: Original Cell-Free Massive MIMO

  Set Dбөў = IвӮҳ for all i. Every AP antenna serves every UE:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ    вҲҖ i, l

  Equations (9) and (10) reduce to (6) and (7) from Section III.

  Case 2: User-Centric Cell-Free Massive MIMO (Buzzi & D'Andrea, 2017 [27])

  Let в„ібөў вҠӮ {1, ..., L} denote the subset of APs that serve UE i. Then:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ    if l вҲҲ в„ібөў        ... (Eq. 11)
  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ    if l вҲү в„ібөў

  This is the AP-level selection: each AP either fully participates or not at
  all (all N antennas together). This is "exactly the setup previously
  considered in [17]" вҖ” the original DCC paper.

  Case 3: Fog Massive MIMO (Bursalioglu et al., 2019 [29])

  The Fog Massive MIMO architecture uses рқ’ңбөў instead of в„ібөў to denote the AP
  subset. Otherwise identical to Case 2 вҖ” it is an instance of DCC.

  Case 4: Traditional Cellular Networks (No Cooperation)

  Set DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ only for the single AP l that "owns" UE i's cell, and DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ
  for all others. Each UE is served by exactly one AP.

  Case 5: Network-Centric Clustering (4G CoMP)

  Partition the APs into disjoint groups рқ’ўвӮҒ, рқ’ўвӮӮ, .... UE i is served by all APs
  in whichever group it belongs to:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ    if l вҲҲ рқ’ўвұј and UE i is in cluster j
  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ    otherwise

  This creates non-overlapping cooperation regions вҖ” the approach that failed in
   4G CoMP.

  Case 6: Per-Antenna Selection

  Set individual diagonal elements of DбөўвӮ— to 0 or 1 independently. This allows
  different antennas at the same AP to serve different UEs вҖ” maximum flexibility
   but rarely used in practice.

  Summary Table:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  2.6 The Two Key Sets: в„ібөў and рқ’ҹвӮ—

  The paper defines two complementary sets that are central to the entire
  framework:

  Set в„ібөў: The set of APs serving UE i (UE-centric view):

  в–Һ в„ібөў = {l : DбөўвӮ— вү  0вӮҷ, l вҲҲ {1,...,L}}

  "Which APs help me?"

  Set рқ’ҹвӮ—: The set of UEs served by AP l (AP-centric view), defined in Eq. (12):

  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮ— = {i : tr(DбөўвӮ—) вүҘ 1, i вҲҲ {1,...,K}}        ... (Eq. 12)

  "Which UEs do I help?"

  These are dual perspectives of the same information:

  в–Һ l вҲҲ в„ібөў  вҹә  i вҲҲ рқ’ҹвӮ—

  Scalability is controlled by |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вҖ” the number of UEs that AP l serves. If
  this is bounded as K вҶ’ вҲһ, the AP's workload is bounded.

  2.7 Section IV-B: Lemma 1 вҖ” Partial Solution to Scalability

  This is the key theoretical result of Section IV:

  в–Һ Lemma 1: If the cardinality |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ for l = 1,...,L, then 
  the Cell-Free Massive MIMO network with DCC satisfies the first three 
  conditions in Definition 1.

  Proof (given in the paper): AP l only needs to:
  1. Estimate channels for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs вҶ’ finite complexity as K вҶ’ вҲһ вң…
  2. Compute combining/precoding for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs вҶ’ finite complexity as K вҶ’ вҲһ вң…
  3. Send/receive fronthaul data for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs вҶ’ finite load as K вҶ’ вҲһ вң…

  The fourth condition (power control) is NOT captured by Lemma 1. However, it
  is "relatively easy to satisfy" вҖ” for example:
  - UL: full power transmission (pбөў = P for all i)
  - DL: equal power allocation among served UEs (ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ)

  These are heuristic but have O(1) complexity per AP.

  Let me formalize the complexity bounds:

  Under Lemma 1, for each AP l:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ         Task          в”Ӯ            Complexity            в”Ӯ    Bound    в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  Everything is O(1) in K вҖ” scalable.

  2.8 The Remaining Challenge

  Lemma 1 says: "If |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is bounded, scalability (criteria 1вҖ“3) follows."

  But how do we ensure |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is bounded while guaranteeing every UE is served?
  This is the question Section V will answer with:
  - Assumption 1: Each AP serves at most one UE per pilot вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ П„вӮҡ
  - A three-step algorithm for joint initial access, pilot assignment, and
  cluster formation

  ---
  3. HISTORICAL CONTEXT AND PRIOR DEVELOPMENTS

  3.1 The DCC Framework вҖ” Origin Story

  BjГ¶rnson, JaldГ©n, Bengtsson, and Ottersten (2011) [17]:
  - Title: "Optimality Properties, Distributed Strategies, and Measurement-Based
   Evaluation of Coordinated Multicell OFDMA Transmission"
  - Published: IEEE Trans. Signal Process., vol. 59, no. 12, pp. 6086вҖ“6101
  - Key innovation: Introduced the "inner circle / outer circle" cooperation
  model where each UE has a personalized set of base stations (BSs) that either
  jointly transmit data (inner circle) or suppress interference (outer circle)
  - Proposed practical distributed beamforming strategies
  - Validated with real measurement data from an LTE-like testbed

  BjГ¶rnson and Jorswieck (2013) [10]:
  - Title: "Optimal Resource Allocation in Coordinated Multi-Cell Systems"
  - Published: Foundations and Trends in Communications and Information Theory,
  vol. 9, no. 2-3
  - Formalized DCC with the diagonal matrices DбөўвӮ—
  - Showed DCC can model: interference channels, cognitive radio, relay
  channels, Network MIMO, coordinated beamforming, and everything in between
  - Provided a complete optimization framework

  3.2 The Failure of Network-Centric Clustering (4G CoMP)

  4G LTE-Advanced (3GPP Release 11, ~2012) introduced Coordinated Multi-Point 
  (CoMP) with three modes:

  1. Joint Transmission (JT): Multiple cells transmit the same data to a UE
  2. Dynamic Point Selection (DPS): The best cell is selected per subframe
  3. Coordinated Scheduling / Coordinated Beamforming (CS/CB): Cells coordinate
  to reduce interference

  All three modes used network-centric (disjoint) clustering вҖ” the APs were
  partitioned into non-overlapping groups.

  Why CoMP failed in practice (only 20вҖ“30% cell-edge gains):
  - Backhaul latency: Sharing CSI between cells required fast backhaul that
  wasn't available
  - Feedback overhead: FDD operation required UEs to feed back CSI вҖ” expensive
  and imprecise
  - Intra-site-only cooperation: Most practical deployments only coordinated
  sectors of the same physical site
  - Disjoint clustering: UEs at cluster edges still suffered inter-cluster
  interference вҖ” the cell-edge problem was merely shifted to cluster edges

  Sources:
  - A. Osseiran, J. F. Monserrat, and P. Marsch, 5G Mobile and Wireless 
  Communications Technology, Cambridge Univ. Press, 2016, Ch. 9 [14]
  - I. D. Garcia et al., "Dynamic cooperation set clustering on BS cooperation
  cellular networks," IEEE PIMRC, 2010 [15]

  3.3 From Disjoint to Overlapping вҖ” The Paradigm Shift

  The critical insight: overlapping clusters are essential.

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ     Approach     в”Ӯ     Cluster      в”Ӯ   Cell-Edge     в”Ӯ   Reference    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ    Structure     в”Ӯ     Problem     в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ No cooperation   в”Ӯ Each UE вҶ’ 1 AP   в”Ӯ Severe          в”Ӯ Traditional    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ                 в”Ӯ cellular       в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Network-centric  в”Ӯ Disjoint groups  в”Ӯ Shifted to      в”Ӯ [11]вҖ“[13]      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ CoMP             в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ cluster edges   в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ DCC              в”Ӯ Overlapping      в”Ӯ Eliminated      в”Ӯ [17], this     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ (user-centric)   в”Ӯ per-UE clusters  в”Ӯ                 в”Ӯ paper          в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The key paper bridging this gap was TГ¶lli, Codreanu, and Juntti (2008) [16]:
  - Title: "Cooperative MIMO-OFDM Cellular System with Soft Handover Between
  Distributed Base Station Antennas"
  - IEEE Trans. Wireless Commun., vol. 7, no. 4
  - First to propose user-specific AP subsets with soft handover between them

  3.4 User-Centric Approaches in the Cell-Free Literature

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ      Paper       в”Ӯ Year в”Ӯ       Approach        в”Ӯ      Limitation       в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”Ӯ Bursalioglu et   в”Ӯ 2019 в”Ӯ Fog Massive MIMO, DL  в”Ӯ Does NOT guarantee    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ al. [29]         в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ only                  в”Ӯ service               в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ This paper       в”Ӯ 2020 в”Ӯ DCC + Assumption 1 +  в”Ӯ Both guaranteed вң…    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ 3-step algorithm      в”Ӯ                       в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  3.5 pCell: The Practical Demonstration

  Artemis Networks' pCell technology [21] (Steve Perlman, 2015) demonstrated
  that DCC-style distributed MIMO is practically feasible:
  - Creates a virtual personal cell for each user
  - Exploits interference constructively through coordinated transmission
  - Real-world demonstrations showed near-theoretical performance
  - Originally called DIDO (Distributed-Input Distributed-Output)

  However, the combination of Network MIMO and DCC "didn't gain much interest at
   the time" because Massive MIMO was simultaneously conceived (Marzetta, 2010)
  and "rightfully gained the spotlight."

  ---
  4. MATHEMATICAL DEEP DIVE

  4.1 The DбөўвӮ— Matrix вҖ” Formal Properties

  DбөўвӮ— вҲҲ в„ӮбҙәЛЈбҙә is a diagonal matrix with binary entries:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = diag(dВ№бөўвӮ—, dВІбөўвӮ—, ..., dбҙәбөўвӮ—),    dКІбөўвӮ— вҲҲ {0, 1}

  Properties:

  1. Idempotent: DбөўвӮ—ВІ = DбөўвӮ— (since each diagonal entry is 0 or 1, and 0ВІ = 0, 1ВІ
   = 1)
  2. Self-adjoint: DбөўвӮ—бҙҙ = DбөўвӮ— (real diagonal вҶ’ Hermitian)
  3. Projection: Since DбөўвӮ— is idempotent and Hermitian, it is an orthogonal 
  projection matrix onto the subspace spanned by the selected antenna
  dimensions.
  4. Trace gives antenna count: tr(DбөўвӮ—) = number of antennas at AP l serving UE
  i.
  5. Zeroing effect: For any vector x вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙә:
  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— x keeps the entries of x corresponding to selected antennas and zeros 
  out the rest.

  4.2 Derivation of UL DCC Signal Model (Equation 9)

  Starting from the received signal at AP l (Eq. 5):

  в–Һ yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + nвӮ—

  AP l applies combining with the DCC-modified vector DвӮ–вӮ— vвӮ–вӮ— (or equivalently,
  vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— since DвӮ–вӮ— is Hermitian):

  в–Һ vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ = vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· hбөўвӮ— sбөў + nвӮ—)

  Summing over all APs:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ

  In collective form:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– (hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– hбөў sбөў + n)

  Expanding:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– В· sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў В· sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n        ... (Eq. 9)

  Note: When DвӮ–вӮ— = 0вӮҷ (AP l does not serve UE k):
  в–Һ vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— = 0бөҖ вҶ’ AP l contributes zero to ЕқвӮ–, regardless of vвӮ–вӮ—

  This means only APs in the set в„івӮ– = {l : DвӮ–вӮ— вү  0вӮҷ} contribute.

  4.3 Derivation of DL DCC Signal Model (Equation 10)

  The transmitted signal at AP l becomes:

  в–Һ xвӮ—бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў

  The DбөўвӮ— matrix is applied before transmission, zeroing out the precoding
  vector for UEs not served by AP l.

  The received signal at UE k:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ— ПӮбөў + nвӮ–

  Rearranging (swap summation order):

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· (вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ—) ПӮбөў + nвӮ–

  Using collective vectors:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ–        ... (Eq. 10)

  Expanding the desired and interference:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– wвӮ– ПӮвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒ,бөўвү вӮ–бҙ· hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ–
  в–Һ         вҺЈвҺҰ             вҺЈ_____________вҺҰ
  в–Һ         desired signal              interference from other UEs

  Important observation about the interference term: The interference from UE i
  is:

  в–Һ hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў wбөў = вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё hвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DбөўвӮ— wбөўвӮ—

  Only APs that serve UE i (those with DбөўвӮ— вү  0вӮҷ) contribute to this
  interference. So UE k only receives interference from APs that are actively 
  serving other UEs вҖ” not from all APs. However, UE k still receives
  interference from UEs served by different APs (through the channel hвӮ–вӮ—), since
   radio waves propagate regardless of DCC assignments.

  4.4 Formal Proof of Lemma 1

  Statement: If |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ for all l, then criteria 1вҖ“3 of
  Definition 1 are satisfied.

  Proof (expanded from the paper):

  Criterion 1 (Channel Estimation): AP l only needs estimates {ДҘвӮ–вӮ— : k вҲҲ рқ’ҹвӮ—}.
  The number of estimates is |рқ’ҹвӮ—|, which is constant. Each estimate requires NВІ
  multiplications (from Section II-A). Total: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| В· NВІ = constant. вң…

  Criterion 2 (Signal Processing):
  - UL: AP l computes {vвӮ–вӮ—бҙҙ DвӮ–вӮ— yвӮ—бөҳЛЎ : k вҲҲ рқ’ҹвӮ—}. Number of operations: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| В· N =
   constant. вң…
  - DL: AP l forms xвӮ—бөҲЛЎ = вҲ‘вӮ–вҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— DвӮ–вӮ— wвӮ–вӮ— ПӮвӮ–. Number of terms: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = constant. вң…
  - Computing combining/precoding vectors: depends on scheme, but input size is
  |рқ’ҹвӮ—| (constant). вң…

  Criterion 3 (Fronthaul): AP l sends/receives data for |рқ’ҹвӮ—| UEs:
  - UL: sends |рқ’ҹвӮ—| complex scalars per time slot вҶ’ constant. вң…
  - DL: receives |рқ’ҹвӮ—| complex scalars per time slot вҶ’ constant. вң…

  Criterion 4 (Power Control): NOT guaranteed by Lemma 1. Network-wide
  optimization still involves all K UEs. Needs separate treatment (heuristic
  algorithms). вҡ пёҸ

  QED в–Ў

  4.5 Showing the Original CF-mMIMO is a Special Case

  When Dбөў = IвӮҳ for all i, let's verify that Eq. (9) reduces to Eq. (6):

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– n

  With DвӮ– = IвӮҳ:

  в–Һ ЕқвӮ– = vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ IвӮҳ n
  в–Һ = vвӮ–бҙҙ hвӮ– sвӮ– + вҲ‘бөўвү вӮ– vвӮ–бҙҙ hбөў sбөў + vвӮ–бҙҙ n        вҶҗ This is Eq. (6) вң“

  Similarly, Eq. (10) with Dбөў = IвӮҳ:

  в–Һ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөў IвӮҳ wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ– = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ–        вҶҗ This is Eq. (7) вң“

  4.6 Showing the User-Centric Approach (Eq. 11) is a Special Case

  When DбөўвӮ— is defined as in Eq. (11):

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ  if l вҲҲ в„ібөў
  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ  if l вҲү в„ібөў

  The collective matrix becomes:

  в–Һ Dбөў = diag(DбөўвӮҒ, ..., DбөўвӮ—)

  with IвӮҷ blocks at positions l вҲҲ в„ібөў and 0вӮҷ blocks elsewhere. Then:

  в–Һ Dбөў wбөў keeps only the components corresponding to APs in в„ібөў and zeros out the
   rest

  This means only APs in в„ібөў contribute to UE i's signal вҖ” exactly the
  user-centric model of [27].

  ---
  5. NUMERICAL EXAMPLES

  Example 1: DCC Matrices in a Small Network

  Setup: L = 4 APs, N = 2 antennas each, K = 3 UEs. Total antennas M = 8.

  Cluster assignments (user-centric, Eq. 11):
  - UE 1: served by APs {1, 2}     вҶ’ в„івӮҒ = {1, 2}
  - UE 2: served by APs {2, 3}     вҶ’ в„івӮӮ = {2, 3}
  - UE 3: served by APs {3, 4}     вҶ’ в„івӮғ = {3, 4}

  The D matrices:

  UE 1:
  в–Һ DвӮҒвӮҒ = IвӮӮ,  DвӮҒвӮӮ = IвӮӮ,  DвӮҒвӮғ = 0вӮӮ,  DвӮҒвӮ„ = 0вӮӮ

  UE 2:
  в–Һ DвӮӮвӮҒ = 0вӮӮ,  DвӮӮвӮӮ = IвӮӮ,  DвӮӮвӮғ = IвӮӮ,  DвӮӮвӮ„ = 0вӮӮ

  UE 3:
  в–Һ DвӮғвӮҒ = 0вӮӮ,  DвӮғвӮӮ = 0вӮӮ,  DвӮғвӮғ = IвӮӮ,  DвӮғвӮ„ = IвӮӮ

  The dual sets рқ’ҹвӮ— (UEs served by each AP):
  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮҒ = {1}         вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮҒ| = 1
  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮӮ = {1, 2}      вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮӮ| = 2
  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮғ = {2, 3}      вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮғ| = 2
  в–Һ рқ’ҹвӮ„ = {3}         вҶ’ |рқ’ҹвӮ„| = 1

  Maximum |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = 2 вҖ” this is constant (independent of K as long as we maintain
  bounded cluster size).

  Overlap: AP 2 serves both UE 1 and UE 2. AP 3 serves both UE 2 and UE 3. These
   are the overlapping clusters вҖ” the hallmark of user-centric DCC.

  Verification: Every UE is served by at least one AP вң…

  Example 2: DL Signal with DCC

  Continuing Example 1. Let N = 1 (single antenna) for simplicity. Channels:

  hвӮҒвӮҒ = 0.8,  hвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.5,  hвӮҒвӮғ = 0.1,  hвӮҒвӮ„ = 0.02
  hвӮӮвӮҒ = 0.1,  hвӮӮвӮӮ = 0.6,  hвӮӮвӮғ = 0.7,  hвӮӮвӮ„ = 0.05
  hвӮғвӮҒ = 0.02, hвӮғвӮӮ = 0.1,  hвӮғвӮғ = 0.4,  hвӮғвӮ„ = 0.9
  Precoding vectors (MR, assume perfect CSI, already normalized so ПҒбөў = 1):
  в–Һ wвӮҒвӮҒ = 0.8,  wвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.5,  wвӮҒвӮғ = 0,  wвӮҒвӮ„ = 0     (only APs 1,2)
  в–Һ wвӮӮвӮҒ = 0,    wвӮӮвӮӮ = 0.6,  wвӮӮвӮғ = 0.7, wвӮӮвӮ„ = 0     (only APs 2,3)
  в–Һ wвӮғвӮҒ = 0,    wвӮғвӮӮ = 0,    wвӮғвӮғ = 0.4, wвӮғвӮ„ = 0.9    (only APs 3,4)

  DL received signal at UE 1 (Eq. 10):

  Desired signal (hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮҒ wвӮҒ):
  в–Һ = hвӮҒвӮҒ* В· DвӮҒвӮҒ В· wвӮҒвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮ* В· DвӮҒвӮӮ В· wвӮҒвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғ* В· DвӮҒвӮғ В· wвӮҒвӮғ + hвӮҒвӮ„* В· DвӮҒвӮ„ В· wвӮҒвӮ„
  в–Һ = 0.8 Г— 1 Г— 0.8 + 0.5 Г— 1 Г— 0.5 + 0.1 Г— 0 Г— 0 + 0.02 Г— 0 Г— 0
  в–Һ = 0.64 + 0.25 = 0.89

  Interference from UE 2 (hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮӮ wвӮӮ):
  в–Һ = hвӮҒвӮҒ* В· DвӮӮвӮҒ В· wвӮӮвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮ* В· DвӮӮвӮӮ В· wвӮӮвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғ* В· DвӮӮвӮғ В· wвӮӮвӮғ + hвӮҒвӮ„* В· DвӮӮвӮ„ В· wвӮӮвӮ„
  в–Һ = 0.8 Г— 0 Г— 0 + 0.5 Г— 1 Г— 0.6 + 0.1 Г— 1 Г— 0.7 + 0.02 Г— 0 Г— 0
  в–Һ = 0 + 0.30 + 0.07 + 0 = 0.37

  Interference from UE 3 (hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮғ wвӮғ):
  в–Һ = hвӮҒвӮҒ* В· DвӮғвӮҒ В· wвӮғвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮ* В· DвӮғвӮӮ В· wвӮғвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғ* В· DвӮғвӮғ В· wвӮғвӮғ + hвӮҒвӮ„* В· DвӮғвӮ„ В· wвӮғвӮ„
  в–Һ = 0.8 Г— 0 Г— 0 + 0.5 Г— 0 Г— 0 + 0.1 Г— 1 Г— 0.4 + 0.02 Г— 1 Г— 0.9
  в–Һ = 0 + 0 + 0.04 + 0.018 = 0.058

  Observations:
  - Desired signal power: |0.89|ВІ = 0.792
  - UE 2 interference: |0.37|ВІ = 0.137 (significant вҖ” AP 2 is shared!)
  - UE 3 interference: |0.058|ВІ = 0.003 (negligible вҖ” no shared APs)
  - The interference is dominated by UEs that share APs with UE 1

  This shows why the P-MMSE scheme (Section V) targets interference from UEs
  with overlapping clusters.

  Example 3: Comparing Architectures via DCC

  Setup: L = 6 APs (numbered 1вҖ“6), K = 4 UEs, N = 1.

  Architecture A: Original CF-mMIMO (all serve all):

  D_{il} = 1 for ALL i,l pairs вҶ’ 6Г—4 = 24 "ones"
  |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = 4 for every AP
  Per-AP fronthaul (UL): 4 scalars/slot
  Architecture B: Disjoint clustering ({APs 1,2,3} = cluster Оұ; {APs 4,5,6} =
  cluster ОІ):

  UEs 1,2 in cluster Оұ; UEs 3,4 in cluster ОІ
  |рқ’ҹвӮҒ| = |рқ’ҹвӮӮ| = |рқ’ҹвӮғ| = 2;  |рқ’ҹвӮ„| = |рқ’ҹвӮ…| = |рқ’ҹвӮҶ| = 2
  Per-AP fronthaul: 2 scalars/slot
  Problem: UE 2 near the boundary вҶ’ strong interference from cluster ОІ вқҢ
  Architecture C: User-centric DCC (each UE selects 2 nearest APs):

  UE 1 вҶ’ {AP 1, AP 2};  UE 2 вҶ’ {AP 3, AP 4};  UE 3 вҶ’ {AP 4, AP 5};  UE 4 вҶ’ {AP
  5, AP 6}
  |рқ’ҹвӮҒ| = 1, |рқ’ҹвӮӮ| = 1, |рқ’ҹвӮғ| = 1, |рқ’ҹвӮ„| = 2, |рқ’ҹвӮ…| = 2, |рқ’ҹвӮҶ| = 1
  Per-AP fronthaul: max 2 scalars/slot
  No hard boundaries вҶ’ no cell-edge problem вң…
  ---
  6. PRACTICE PROBLEMS

  Problem 1: Constructing DCC Matrices

  A network has L = 5 APs, K = 3 UEs, N = 2. The cluster assignments are:
  - в„івӮҒ = {1, 2, 3}  (UE 1 served by APs 1, 2, 3)
  - в„івӮӮ = {2, 3, 4}  (UE 2 served by APs 2, 3, 4)
  - в„івӮғ = {4, 5}     (UE 3 served by APs 4, 5)

  (a) Write out all DбөўвӮ— matrices (using Eq. 11).
  (b) Compute the sets рқ’ҹвӮ— for each AP.
  (c) What is max_l |рқ’ҹвӮ—|? Is it bounded (independent of K)?
  (d) Verify that every UE is served by at least one AP.

  Solutions:

  (a) Using Eq. (11): DбөўвӮ— = IвӮӮ if l вҲҲ в„ібөў, 0вӮӮ otherwise.

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ AP 1 в”Ӯ AP 2 в”Ӯ AP 3 в”Ӯ AP 4 в”Ӯ AP 5 в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 1 в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 2 в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 3 в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ 0вӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ IвӮӮ   в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  (b) рқ’ҹвӮҒ = {1}, рқ’ҹвӮӮ = {1,2}, рқ’ҹвӮғ = {1,2}, рқ’ҹвӮ„ = {2,3}, рқ’ҹвӮ… = {3}

  (c) max_l |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = 2 (APs 2, 3, and 4 each serve 2 UEs). This is bounded and
  independent of K. вң…

  (d) |в„івӮҒ| = 3 вүҘ 1 вң…, |в„івӮӮ| = 3 вүҘ 1 вң…, |в„івӮғ| = 2 вүҘ 1 вң…. All UEs are served.

  Problem 2: Scalability Comparison

  Consider a network with L = 100 APs, N = 4, П„вӮҡ = 10.

  (a) Original CF-mMIMO (all serve all): What are |рқ’ҹвӮ—| and the per-AP estimation
   complexity for K = 500?
  (b) User-centric DCC with each AP serving at most П„вӮҡ = 10 UEs: Same questions
  for K = 500.
  (c) What if K grows to 5,000? Recompute both cases.

  Solutions:

  (a) Original: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = K = 500. Estimation: 500 Г— NВІ = 500 Г— 16 = 8,000
  multiplications/AP.

  (b) DCC: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ П„вӮҡ = 10. Estimation: 10 Г— 16 = 160 multiplications/AP. (50Г—
  less!)

  (c) K = 5,000:
  - Original: 5,000 Г— 16 = 80,000 multiplications/AP (10Г— increase from K=500)
  - DCC: Still 10 Г— 16 = 160 multiplications/AP (unchanged!) вҶҗ This is 
  scalability

  Problem 3: DL Interference Analysis with DCC

  Setup: L = 3 APs, N = 1, K = 2 UEs. в„івӮҒ = {1, 2}, в„івӮӮ = {2, 3}.

  Channels: hвӮҒвӮҒ = 0.7, hвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.4, hвӮҒвӮғ = 0.05, hвӮӮвӮҒ = 0.1, hвӮӮвӮӮ = 0.5, hвӮӮвӮғ = 0.8.

  MR precoding (unnormalized for simplicity): wбөўвӮ— = hбөўвӮ— for l вҲҲ в„ібөў, 0 otherwise.

  (a) Compute the desired signal gain for UE 1: |hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮҒ wвӮҒ|
  (b) Compute the interference from UE 2 on UE 1: |hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮӮ wвӮӮ|
  (c) Which AP causes the interference overlap? Why?
  (d) Compare with the original CF-mMIMO case (Dбөў = IвӮғ вҲҖi): recompute (a) and
  (b).

  Solutions:

  (a) hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮҒ wвӮҒ = hвӮҒвӮҒВ·wвӮҒвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮВ·wвӮҒвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғВ·0 = 0.7Г—0.7 + 0.4Г—0.4 = 0.49 + 0.16 =
  0.65

  (b) hвӮҒбҙҙ DвӮӮ wвӮӮ = hвӮҒвӮҒВ·0 + hвӮҒвӮӮВ·wвӮӮвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғВ·wвӮӮвӮғ = 0 + 0.4Г—0.5 + 0.05Г—0.8 = 0.20 +
  0.04 = 0.24

  (c) AP 2 causes the interference overlap. It serves both UE 1 and UE 2, so
  when it transmits to UE 2 (with precoding wвӮӮвӮӮ = 0.5), UE 1 receives this
  through channel hвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.4. AP 3 contributes negligible interference (hвӮҒвӮғ =
  0.05 is very weak).

  (d) Original CF-mMIMO (Dбөў = IвӮғ):
  - Desired: hвӮҒвӮҒВ·hвӮҒвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮВ·hвӮҒвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғВ·hвӮҒвӮғ = 0.49 + 0.16 + 0.0025 = 0.6525
  (slightly more)
  - Interference: hвӮҒвӮҒВ·hвӮӮвӮҒ + hвӮҒвӮӮВ·hвӮӮвӮӮ + hвӮҒвӮғВ·hвӮӮвӮғ = 0.07 + 0.20 + 0.04 = 0.31 (29%
  more interference!)

  The DCC reduces interference more than it reduces the desired signal вҶ’ net
  benefit from user-centric clustering.

  в”Ӯ innovation    в”Ӯ                                                         в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ DL with DCC   в”Ӯ yвӮ–бөҲЛЎ = hвӮ–бҙҙ вҲ‘бөў Dбөў wбөў ПӮбөў + nвӮ– (Eq. 10)                    в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Special cases в”Ӯ Original CF = Dбөў = IвӮҳ; User-centric = DбөўвӮ— вҲҲ {IвӮҷ, 0вӮҷ}    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ per Eq. (11)                                            в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Two key sets  в”Ӯ в„ібөў = APs serving UE i; рқ’ҹвӮ— = UEs served by AP l          в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Lemma 1       в”Ӯ If |рқ’ҹвӮ—| is constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ вҶ’ criteria 1вҖ“3 of          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ scalability satisfied                                   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Remaining gap в”Ӯ Power control (criterion 4) needs heuristic algorithms  в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Historical    в”Ӯ DCC from BjГ¶rnson et al. 2011 [17], formalized in [10]; в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ root          в”Ӯ  CoMP (disjoint) failed in 4G                           в”Ӯ

  ---
  SECTION V-A: ALGORITHM FOR JOINT INITIAL ACCESS, PILOT ASSIGNMENT, AND CLUSTER
   FORMATION

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  (Section V is split into sub-sections due to its length. This covers Section 
  V-A and the foundational Assumption 1.)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  Imagine you just moved to a new city and need to sign up for pizza delivery
  service. Here's how the process works in three simple steps:

  Step 1 вҖ” You pick your "main driver" (Master AP):
  You look around and find which driver is closest to your house (strongest
  signal). You call that driver and say: "You're my main driver now." This
  driver is required to serve you вҖ” no matter what. This guarantees you won't be
   left without service.

  Step 2 вҖ” The main driver gives you a "code" (Pilot Assignment):
  There are only a limited number of delivery codes (say, 10 colors: red, blue,
  green...). Your main driver checks which code has the least traffic in the
  area and assigns that code to you. Then the driver tells nearby drivers: "Hey,
   I'm serving this new customer on code Blue."

  Step 3 вҖ” Nearby drivers decide whether to also serve you (Cluster Formation):
  Each nearby driver checks: "Am I already serving someone on code Blue?" If
  not, they volunteer to also serve you. If they are already serving someone on
  Blue but your house is closer (better channel), they switch to you and drop
  the farther customer (who still has their main driver).

  Why this works:
  - Every customer is guaranteed service вҖ” the main driver must serve them (no
  orphans)
  - Each driver serves at most 10 customers (one per code) вҖ” scalable!
  - Everything is local вҖ” no central authority needed; each driver makes
  decisions based only on nearby information
  - The clusters overlap naturally вҖ” neighboring drivers serve overlapping sets
  of customers

  The key rule (Assumption 1): Each driver serves at most one customer per code.
   Since there are only П„вӮҡ codes, each driver serves at most П„вӮҡ customers. This
  is the mechanism that guarantees scalability.

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 Assumption 1: The Foundation of Scalability

  Before describing the algorithm, the paper introduces the crucial design
  constraint:

  в–Һ Assumption 1: Each AP serves at most one UE per pilot sequence and uses all 
  its N antennas to serve these UEs.

  Mathematically, this implies:

  в–Һ |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ П„вӮҡ        for all l = 1, ..., L

  and:

  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = IвӮҷ    if i вҲҲ рқ’ҹвӮ—
  в–Һ DбөўвӮ— = 0вӮҷ    if i вҲү рқ’ҹвӮ—            ... (Eq. 13)

  Three rationales for this assumption:

  Rationale 1 вҖ” Avoiding intra-AP pilot contamination: If AP l served two UEs,
  say UE k and UE j, on the same pilot t, then both channel estimates ДҘвӮ–вӮ— and
  ДҘвұјвӮ— would be derived from the identical received pilot signal yвӮңвӮ—бө–вҒұЛЎбө’бө—. The
  estimates would be strongly correlated, and the AP would be unable to
  distinguish their channels. When it precodes toward one, it would
  inadvertently create strong coherent interference toward the other. This
  coherent interference scales with N вҖ” exactly the same rate as the desired
  signal вҖ” making it devastating.

  By serving at most one UE per pilot, the AP avoids this intra-AP pilot
  contamination problem entirely.

  Rationale 2 вҖ” Fixed, scalable complexity: Since П„вӮҡ is a constant (independent
  of K), the bound |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ П„вӮҡ is automatically constant as K вҶ’ вҲһ. By Lemma 1 from
   Section IV, this guarantees that the first three scalability criteria
  (estimation, processing, fronthaul) are satisfied.

  Rationale 3 вҖ” Predictable fronthaul requirements: Each AP needs to support at
  most П„вӮҡ parallel UL and DL data streams over its fronthaul link. This is a
  fixed, designable requirement.

  The trade-off: In areas with dense UEs, some APs cannot serve all nearby UEs
  (they run out of pilot slots). Those UEs receive less macro-diversity (fewer
  serving APs) вҖ” the price for provable scalability. However, each UE is still
  guaranteed service by at least its Master AP.

  2.2 The Three-Step Algorithm

  The paper proposes a three-step procedure for when a new UE (indexed K+1)
  wants to access the network. The procedure is illustrated in Fig. 3 of the
  paper.

  Step 1: The UE Appoints a Master AP

  The accessing UE measures the large-scale fading coefficient ОІвӮ— from all
  nearby APs:

  в–Һ ОІвӮ— = tr(RвӮҚвӮ–вӮҠвӮҒвӮҺвӮ—) / N        for all nearby APs l

  How does the UE measure ОІвӮ—? Using periodically broadcasted synchronization 
  signals from the APs. In 5G NR, these are:
  - PSS (Primary Synchronization Signal): Enables coarse time/frequency
  synchronization and identifies the cell-ID group
  - SSS (Secondary Synchronization Signal): Enables fine synchronization and
  identifies the complete cell ID
  - SS/PBCH block: Carries the synchronization signals and basic system
  information

  The UE receives these signals from multiple APs, measures the received power
  (which is proportional to ОІвӮ—), and selects:

  в–Һ в„“ = argmaxвӮ— ОІвӮ—            ... (Eq. 14)

  as its Master AP вҖ” the AP with the strongest average channel.

  The UE also synchronizes to the Master AP using the broadcast signal, then
  contacts it via a standard random access procedure (RACH):

  In 5G NR, the RACH procedure has four steps:
  1. UE sends a random preamble on PRACH (Physical Random Access Channel)
  2. AP responds with a Random Access Response (RAR)
  3. UE sends its identity and connection request
  4. AP confirms the connection (contention resolution)

  Why the Master AP concept is critical: It guarantees that every UE is served 
  by at least one AP. Previous user-centric approaches [27], [29] had the risk
  that a UE could be inadvertently dropped from service because no AP decided to
   serve it. The Master AP concept flips the initiative: the UE appoints its AP,
   not the other way around.

  Source: S. Sesia, I. Toufik, and M. Baker, LTE вҖ” The UMTS Long Term Evolution:
   From Theory to Practice, Wiley, 2009 [42].

  Step 2: The Master AP Assigns a Pilot and Notifies Neighbors

  The appointed Master AP responds by assigning pilot П„ to the new UE, chosen
  as:

  в–Һ П„ = argminвӮң tr(ОЁвӮңвӮ—)            ... (Eq. 15)

  where ОЁвӮңвӮ— is the correlation matrix of the received pilot signal (from Eq. 4):

  в–Һ ОЁвӮңвӮ— = вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’®вӮң П„вӮҡ pбөў RбөўвӮ— + ПғВІ IвӮҷ

  Recall that tr(ОЁвӮңвӮ—) = вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’®вӮң П„вӮҡ pбөў tr(RбөўвӮ—) + NПғВІ is the total received pilot 
  power on pilot t at AP l. So Eq. (15) selects the pilot where the Master AP
  observes the least pilot contamination.

  Why this criterion? Lower tr(ОЁвӮңвӮ—) means:
  - Fewer or weaker interfering UEs on that pilot (as seen by this AP)
  - Better channel estimation quality (ДҘвӮ–вӮ— will have lower MSE)
  - Less coherent interference in subsequent data transmission

  Important detail: The computation in Eq. (15) only involves the existing K
  UEs. The Master AP already knows {ОЁвӮңвӮ—} from its current operation вҖ” no
  additional communication is needed.

  After assigning the pilot: The Master AP informs a limited set of neighboring 
  APs that it is going to serve UE K+1 on pilot П„. This invitation triggers Step
   3.

  Footnote 5 from the paper: The pilot should be one on which the AP is not
  currently serving a UE as Master AP (that role has higher priority). Each AP
  can be the Master AP of at most П„вӮҡ UEs. In the unlikely event this cannot be
  satisfied, multiple UEs can be assigned the same pilot but multiplexed in time
   and/or frequency.

  Step 3: Neighboring APs Decide Whether to Serve the New UE

  Each neighboring AP that receives the invitation makes a local, autonomous 
  decision:

  в–Һ Decision rule: Serve UE K+1 if EITHER:
  в–Һ (a) The AP does not currently serve any UE on pilot П„, OR
  в–Һ (b) The new UE has a better channel (higher ОІвӮ—) than the UE it currently 
  serves on pilot П„, in which case it switches to the new UE.

  Case (a): The AP has a free pilot slot вҖ” it simply adds UE K+1 to its service
  set рқ’ҹвӮ—.

  Case (b): The AP is already full on pilot П„. But if the new UE has a stronger
  channel (closer, less pathloss), the AP drops the current UE on that pilot and
   replaces it with the new one. The dropped UE is not left without service вҖ” it
   still has its Master AP (and potentially other serving APs).

  Why this works for scalability: Each AP makes a decision based on local 
  information only (its own channel measurements). No global coordination is
  needed. The decision only involves comparing two ОІ values вҖ” constant-time
  operation.

  2.3 Putting It All Together

  Summary of the three steps:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ  STEP 1: UE вҶ’ Master AP                                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ                                                  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  UE measures ОІвӮ— from synchronization signals of nearby APs              в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  UE selects: в„“ = argmaxвӮ— ОІвӮ—  (strongest channel)                       в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  UE contacts Master AP в„“ via RACH                                       в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  STEP 2: Master AP вҶ’ Pilot Assignment + Neighbor Notification           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Master AP selects: П„ = argminвӮң tr(ОЁвӮңвӮ—)  (least contaminated pilot)    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Master AP assigns pilot П„ to UE                                        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Master AP informs neighboring APs about the new UE on pilot П„          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ                                  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Each neighbor checks its pilot slot П„:                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ    вҖў Empty? вҶ’ Serve the new UE вң“                                        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ    вҖў Occupied by weaker UE? вҶ’ Switch to new UE вң“                        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ    вҖў Occupied by stronger UE? вҶ’ Decline вң—                               в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  2.4 Properties of the Algorithm

  Property 1 вҖ” Service guarantee: Every UE is served by at least its Master AP.
  No UE can be orphaned.

  Property 2 вҖ” Scalability: Under Assumption 1, each AP serves at most П„вӮҡ UEs.
  Since П„вӮҡ is independent of K:
  - Channel estimation: at most П„вӮҡ estimates per AP вҶ’ O(1) вң…
  - Combining/precoding: at most П„вӮҡ vectors per AP вҶ’ O(1) вң…
  - Fronthaul: at most П„вӮҡ data streams per AP вҶ’ O(1) вң…

  Property 3 вҖ” Distributed operation: Each step uses only local information:
  - Step 1: UE uses locally received synchronization signals
  - Step 2: Master AP uses its own ОЁвӮңвӮ— matrices (already available)
  - Step 3: Each neighboring AP uses its own ОІ values

  No global coordination, no network-wide optimization, no central controller
  needed.

  Property 4 вҖ” Dynamic adaptation: When a UE moves or other UEs
  connect/disconnect:
  - The UE can appoint a new Master AP by repeating Step 1
  - The new Master AP informs the previous one that it has taken over
  - The current Master AP can periodically recompute Eq. (15) to check if a
  different pilot would reduce contamination

  2.5 Comparison with Prior Approaches

  The paper identifies two deficiencies in previous user-centric clustering
  algorithms:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ             Paper              в”Ӯ               Deficiency               в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Ngo et al. [28], Interdonato   в”Ӯ Do not limit how many UEs each AP      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ et al. [33]                    в”Ӯ serves вҶ’ unscalable as K вҶ’ вҲһ           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Buzzi & D'Andrea [27],         в”Ӯ Do not guarantee that all UEs are      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ Bursalioglu et al. [29]        в”Ӯ served вҶ’ UEs may be dropped            в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The proposed algorithm resolves both issues simultaneously.

  2.6 Remark 2: Synchronization Concerns

  The paper notes a practical limitation: the DL signal model in Eq. (10)
  assumes perfect synchronization of all transmissions, which is infeasible due
  to propagation delays. However:

  - If every AP is synchronized with its neighbors (local synchronization)
  - And the UE synchronizes with its Master AP in Step 1

  ...then the dominant terms (from nearby APs with strong channels) in Eq. (10)
  will be accurately aligned. Signals from distant APs (weak channels) may
  arrive with timing offsets, but they contribute little power anyway. So the
  model is "reasonable for analysis."

  ---
  3. HISTORICAL CONTEXT AND PRIOR DEVELOPMENTS

  3.1 Initial Access in Cellular Networks: A Brief History

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ  Era  в”Ӯ                   Mechanism                    в”Ӯ   Reference   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
