  3.3 Why Network-Wide Optimization Is Unscalable

  Network-wide power control couples all K UEs:

  Max-min fairness [5]: Solve a sequence of SOCPs, each with K power variables
  and KL coupling constraints. Interior-point methods: O((KL)^{3.5}) per
  iteration. For K = 1000, L = 400: a single iteration involves ~10^{12}
  operations вҖ” impractical for real-time processing within one coherence block
  (~10 Ојs at 20 MHz).

  Semi-distributed via dual decomposition [10, Sec. 4.3]: Decompose the global
  problem into per-AP subproblems. But:
  - Convergence is slow (hundreds of iterations)
  - Each iteration requires inter-AP message passing (backhaul signaling)
  - More optimization variables than the centralized version
  - "Neither practical nor scalable" (the paper's own assessment)

  ---
  4. MATHEMATICAL DEEP DIVE

  4.1 Proving the Per-AP Constraint Is Satisfied (Centralized, Equal Power)

  With centralized precoding using Eq. (33) with ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ and normalized wМ„бөў:

  AP l's total transmit power:

  в–Һ PвӮ— = вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— рқ”ј{вҖ–wбөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ}
  в–Һ = вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— ПҒбөў рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ}
  в–Һ = (ПҒ/П„вӮҡ) вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ}

  Since вҲ‘вӮ—вӮҢвӮҒбҙё рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ} = рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвҖ–ВІ} = 1, we have рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ} вүӨ 1 for each l.
  Therefore:

  в–Һ PвӮ— вүӨ (ПҒ/П„вӮҡ) Г— |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ (ПҒ/П„вӮҡ) Г— П„вӮҡ = ПҒ вң“

  The bound is achieved only if each UE concentrates all its precoding energy at
   AP l вҖ” which never happens in practice (UEs are served by multiple APs). So
  the actual power is significantly below ПҒ, meaning this is a conservative
  allocation.

  4.2 Verifying the Fractional DL Allocation (Equation 43)

  AP l's total transmit power with Eq. (43):

  в–Һ PвӮ— = вҲ‘вӮ–вҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— ПҒвӮ–вӮ— = вҲ‘вӮ–вҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— ПҒ В· вҲҡОІвӮ–вӮ— / (вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— пҝҪпҝҪОІбөўвӮ—)
  в–Һ = ПҒ В· (вҲ‘вӮ–вҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— вҲҡОІвӮ–вӮ—) / (вҲ‘бөўвҲҲрқ’ҹвӮ— вҲҡОІбөўвӮ—)
  в–Һ = ПҒ вң“

  The AP exactly uses its full power budget вҖ” no waste. This is more
  power-efficient than the equal allocation in the centralized case.

  4.3 Why вҲҡОІвӮ–вӮ— and Not ОІвӮ–вӮ—?

  The choice of вҲҡОІвӮ–вӮ— (rather than ОІвӮ–вӮ—) in Eq. (43) is a design heuristic. Let's
  examine what different exponents would give:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ Allocation ПҒвӮ–вӮ— в”Ӯ           Behavior            в”Ӯ          Name          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ        вҲқ       в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ                        в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ ОІвӮ–вӮ—вҒ° = 1       в”Ӯ Equal power to all served UEs в”Ӯ Equal allocation       в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ ОІвӮ–вӮ—^{1/2}      в”Ӯ Moderate emphasis on strong   в”Ӯ Eq. (43), this paper   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ channels                      в”Ӯ                        в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ ОІвӮ–вӮ—В№           в”Ӯ Strong emphasis on strong     в”Ӯ Channel-gain           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ channels                      в”Ӯ proportional           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ ОІвӮ–вӮ—вҒ»В№          в”Ӯ More power to weak channels   в”Ӯ Inverse-channel        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ (fairness)                    в”Ӯ allocation             в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The вҲҡОІвӮ–вӮ— choice is a compromise: it gives more power to strong channels
  (efficient use of power) without completely neglecting weak channels (some
  fairness). The paper notes that "each AP allocates more power to UEs with
  strong channels than to UEs with weak channels, while guaranteeing non-zero
  powers to all the served UEs."

  4.4 Why the CPU Is a Set of Tasks

  For UE k with Master AP в„“, the "CPU tasks" can be distributed as:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ       Task       в”Ӯ         Who does it          в”Ӯ  Information needed   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ DL data encoding в”Ӯ Master AP в„“ or edge-cloud    в”Ӯ Source bits for UE k  в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UL data decoding в”Ӯ Master AP в„“ or edge-cloud    в”Ӯ Soft estimates from   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                  в”Ӯ                              в”Ӯ APs in в„івӮ–             в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Channel          в”Ӯ Each AP l вҲҲ в„івӮ– locally       в”Ӯ Local pilot signals   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ estimation       в”Ӯ (distributed case)           в”Ӯ                       в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Precoding        в”Ӯ Each AP l вҲҲ в„івӮ– locally       в”Ӯ Local channel         в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ computation      в”Ӯ (distributed case)           в”Ӯ estimates             в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  In the distributed case, the Master AP can handle encoding/decoding, and each
  serving AP handles estimation and precoding independently. The only data
  flowing over fronthaul is:
  - UL: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| soft estimates per time slot from AP l to the Master APs of served
  UEs
  - DL: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| data symbols per time slot from Master APs to AP l

  This is bounded by П„вӮҡ per time slot вҖ” regardless of network size.

  ---
  5. NUMERICAL EXAMPLES

  Example 1: DL Fractional Power Allocation (Eq. 43)

  Setup: AP l serves 3 UEs (|рқ’ҹвӮ—| = 3), maximum power ПҒ = 1 W.

  Channel gains: ОІвӮҒвӮ— = 0.020, ОІвӮӮвӮ— = 0.005, ОІвӮғвӮ— = 0.001.

  Step 1: Compute вҲҡОІбөўвӮ—:
  в–Һ вҲҡОІвӮҒвӮ— = вҲҡ0.020 = 0.1414
  в–Һ вҲҡОІвӮӮвӮ— = вҲҡ0.005 = 0.0707
  в–Һ вҲҡОІвӮғвӮ— = вҲҡ0.001 = 0.0316

  Step 2: Compute the sum:
  в–Һ вҲ‘ = 0.1414 + 0.0707 + 0.0316 = 0.2437

  Step 3: Compute per-UE power:
  в–Һ ПҒвӮҒвӮ— = 1.0 Г— 0.1414/0.2437 = 0.580 W (58.0%)
  в–Һ ПҒвӮӮвӮ— = 1.0 Г— 0.0707/0.2437 = 0.290 W (29.0%)
  в–Һ ПҒвӮғвӮ— = 1.0 Г— 0.0316/0.2437 = 0.130 W (13.0%)

  Verification: 0.580 + 0.290 + 0.130 = 1.000 W = ПҒ пҝҪпҝҪ

  Interpretation: UE 1 (strongest channel, ОІвӮҒвӮ— = 0.020) gets 4.5Г— more power
  than UE 3 (weakest channel, ОІвӮғвӮ— = 0.001). This is because the channel gain
  ratio is ОІвӮҒвӮ—/ОІвӮғвӮ— = 20, but the power ratio is only вҲҡ20 вүҲ 4.5 (the square root
  softens the allocation).

  Compare with equal allocation: Each would get ПҒ/3 = 0.333 W. The fractional
  scheme gives 74% more to UE 1 and 61% less to UE 3.

  Example 2: Centralized vs Distributed Power Efficiency

  Setup: L = 4 APs, П„вӮҡ = 5, ПҒ = 1 W per AP.

  Centralized (equal): ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ = 0.2 W per UE. Each UE's precoding energy is
  distributed across its serving APs.

  Suppose UE k is served by 3 APs with рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„вӮ–вӮ—вҖ–ВІ} = [0.5, 0.3, 0.2] at the three
  APs.

  Power from AP 1 for UE k: 0.2 Г— 0.5 = 0.1 W
  Power from AP 2 for UE k: 0.2 Г— 0.3 = 0.06 W
  Power from AP 3 for UE k: 0.2 Г— 0.2 = 0.04 W

  If AP 1 serves 4 UEs total with similar energy distributions, AP 1's total: ~4
   Г— 0.1 = 0.4 W << 1 W. The AP is underutilized вҖ” significant power waste.

  Distributed (fractional): Each AP fully uses its budget ПҒ = 1 W, distributed
  among its served UEs proportionally to вҲҡОІбөўвӮ—. No power waste.

  This power efficiency gap explains why distributed precoding sometimes
  achieves competitive SE despite having less coordination вҖ” it uses
  significantly more total power (the paper notes "40 times more transmit power"
   in some setups).

  Example 3: Network Topology вҖ” Master AP as CPU

  Setup: L = 6 APs, K = 4 UEs. UE assignments:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ  UE  в”Ӯ Master AP в”Ӯ Serving APs в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 1 в”Ӯ AP 2      в”Ӯ {1, 2, 3}   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 2 в”Ӯ AP 3      в”Ӯ {3, 4}      в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 3 в”Ӯ AP 5      в”Ӯ {4, 5, 6}   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UE 4 в”Ӯ AP 1      в”Ӯ {1, 2}      в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  With Master AP handling CPU tasks:

  - AP 2 handles encoding/decoding for UE 1: receives soft estimates from APs
  {1, 3}
  - AP 3 handles encoding/decoding for UE 2: receives soft estimate from AP {4}
  - AP 5 handles encoding/decoding for UE 3: receives soft estimates from APs
  {4, 6}
  - AP 1 handles encoding/decoding for UE 4: receives soft estimate from AP {2}

  No physical CPU exists. Each AP acts as both a serving AP and (for its Master
  UEs) a local CPU. The fronthaul connections are between neighboring APs only вҖ”
   fully distributed.

  Data flow for UE 1 (UL):
  1. APs 1, 2, 3 each compute local soft estimates: ЕқвӮҒвӮҒ, ЕқвӮҒвӮӮ, ЕқвӮҒвӮғ
  2. APs 1 and 3 send their estimates to Master AP 2
  3. AP 2 computes: ЕқвӮҒ = ЕқвӮҒвӮҒ + ЕқвӮҒвӮӮ + ЕқвӮҒвӮғ and decodes UE 1's data

  Data flow for UE 1 (DL):
  1. AP 2 (Master) encodes UE 1's data symbol ПӮвӮҒ
  2. AP 2 sends ПӮвӮҒ to APs 1 and 3
  3. Each AP applies its local precoding and transmits

  ---
  6. PRACTICE PROBLEMS

  Problem 1: Fractional DL Power Allocation

  AP l serves 4 UEs with ОІ values: ОІвӮҒвӮ— = 0.04, ОІвӮӮвӮ— = 0.01, ОІвӮғвӮ— = 0.0025, ОІвӮ„вӮ— =
  0.0004. Maximum AP power ПҒ = 2 W.

  (a) Compute ПҒвӮ–вӮ— for each UE using Eq. (43).
  (b) Verify вҲ‘вӮ– ПҒвӮ–вӮ— = ПҒ.
  (c) What fraction of the total power does the strongest UE receive?
  (d) If instead equal allocation is used (ПҒвӮ–вӮ— = ПҒ/4), how much does each UE
  get?

  Solutions:

  (a) вҲҡОІвӮҒвӮ— = 0.2, вҲҡОІвӮӮвӮ— = 0.1, вҲҡОІвӮғвӮ— = 0.05, вҲҡОІвӮ„вӮ— = 0.02. Sum = 0.37.

  в–Һ ПҒвӮҒвӮ— = 2 Г— 0.2/0.37 = 1.081 W
  в–Һ ПҒвӮӮвӮ— = 2 Г— 0.1/0.37 = 0.541 W
  в–Һ ПҒвӮғвӮ— = 2 Г— 0.05/0.37 = 0.270 W
  в–Һ ПҒвӮ„вӮ— = 2 Г— 0.02/0.37 = 0.108 W

  (b) 1.081 + 0.541 + 0.270 + 0.108 = 2.000 W = ПҒ вң“

  (c) UE 1: 1.081/2.0 = 54.1% of total power.

  (d) Equal: ПҒвӮ–вӮ— = 2/4 = 0.5 W each. UE 1 goes from 1.081 W to 0.5 W (вҲ’54%), UE
  4 goes from 0.108 W to 0.5 W (+363%).

  Problem 2: Centralized Power Constraint Verification

  П„вӮҡ = 8, ПҒ = 1 W. AP l serves |рқ’ҹвӮ—| = 6 UEs with centralized equal allocation ПҒбөў
   = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ = 0.125 W.

  (a) What is the maximum total power AP l can transmit?
  (b) If each served UE distributes its precoding energy equally across 4 APs,
  what is AP l's actual power?
  (c) How much power is "wasted" (unused)?

  Solutions:

  (a) Maximum: |рқ’ҹвӮ—| Г— ПҒбөў Г— max(рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ}) = 6 Г— 0.125 Г— 1 = 0.75 W (if all
  energy at AP l). But рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ} вүӨ 1 and the bound вүӨ ПҒ = 1 W.

  (b) If each UE's precoding is spread over 4 APs equally: рқ”ј{вҖ–wМ„бөўвӮ—вҖ–ВІ} вүҲ 1/4 =
  0.25. AP l's power: 6 Г— 0.125 Г— 0.25 = 0.1875 W.

  (c) Wasted: ПҒ вҲ’ 0.1875 = 0.8125 W (81.25% unused!). This shows the centralized
   equal allocation can be very conservative.

  Problem 3: Topology Design

  A city has 1000 APs and 500 UEs. П„вӮҡ = 10.

  (a) In the star topology (single CPU), how many data streams must the CPU
  handle per UL time slot?
  (b) With the Master AP approach (distributed), how many data streams does each
   AP handle at most?
  (c) If we use 10 edge-cloud processors, each handling 100 APs, what is each
  processor's load?

  Solutions:

  (a) Star: Each AP sends |рқ’ҹвӮ—| вүӨ 10 scalars per slot. Total: up to 1000 Г— 10 =
  10,000 streams at the CPU.

  (b) Master AP: Each AP handles its own processing + Master duties. As Master
  for at most П„вӮҡ = 10 UEs, it receives soft estimates from each UE's cluster
  APs. Per Master UE: |в„івӮ–| вҲ’ 1 incoming streams (from other serving APs). If
  |в„івӮ–| вүҲ 5: ~40 incoming streams plus 10 local computations. Total вүҲ 50 
  streams/AP вҖ” bounded.

  (c) Each processor handles 100 APs Г— 10 UEs/AP = up to 1000 streams вҖ” 10Г— less
   than the single CPU. And this doesn't grow with K.

  ---
  7. SECTION SUMMARY

  в”Ӯ Scalability      в”Ӯ Both UL and DL schemes are O(1) per AP вҖ” no          в”Ӯ

  finding that scalable processing achieves nearly the same SE as unscalable

в—Ҹ Now here is the comprehensive Section VI explanation.

  ---
  SECTION VI: NUMERICAL ANALYSIS

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  All the theory from Sections IвҖ“V is meaningless unless it actually works in
  practice. This section puts the proposed scalable framework to the test using
  computer simulations.

  Think of it as a race between different strategies:
  - The champions (unscalable): Optimal MMSE and L-MMSE combining вҖ” the best
  possible performance, but impossible to deploy in large networks.
  - The contender (scalable): The paper's new P-MMSE and LP-MMSE schemes.
  - The old default (scalable but weak): MR (maximum ratio) combining from the
  original Cell-Free papers.

  The big question: How much performance do we sacrifice for scalability?

  The answer: Almost nothing!
  - In the uplink: Scalable P-MMSE achieves 89% of optimal MMSE's SE. LP-MMSE is
   2.7Г— better than MR.
  - In the downlink: Scalable LP-MMSE achieves 90% of the best possible
  (genie-aided) SE. MR only gets 60%.

  The simulations test two network configurations:
  - 400 single-antenna APs (lots of small routers)
  - 100 four-antenna APs (fewer but more capable routers)

  Both have 100 users and the same total number of antennas (400). The key
  finding: many single-antenna APs are better for the weakest users (more
  diversity from having APs everywhere), while fewer multi-antenna APs are
  better for the strongest users (local interference suppression at each AP).

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 Simulation Setup

  The paper considers a carefully designed simulation scenario:

  Network geometry:
  - Coverage area: 2 Г— 2 km square
  - Wrap-around technique: The area is tiled to approximate an infinitely large
  network, eliminating boundary effects. A UE near the edge "sees" APs that are
  actually on the opposite side, as if the area were a torus.
  - APs and UEs are independently and uniformly distributed at random

  Two configurations (same total antennas M = 400):

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ   Config   в”Ӯ APs (L) в”Ӯ Antennas/AP (N) в”Ӯ Total antennas (M) в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Setup (i)  в”Ӯ 400     в”Ӯ 1               в”Ӯ 400                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Setup (ii) в”Ӯ 100     в”Ӯ 4               в”Ӯ 400                в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  - K = 100 UEs (single antenna each)
  - Antenna density: 400 / (2Г—2) = 100 antennas/kmВІ
  - UE density: 100 / (2Г—2) = 25 UEs/kmВІ

  Propagation model:
  - Uses the model from [2, Sec. 4.1.3] вҖ” the comprehensive Massive MIMO
  monograph
  - Spatially correlated fading: not i.i.d. Rayleigh вҖ” realistic spatial
  correlation
  - APs deployed 10 m above UEs (creates a natural minimum 3D distance, avoiding
   unrealistically strong channels)
  - Correlated Rayleigh fading with the local scattering model from the
  monograph

  System parameters:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ        Parameter         в”Ӯ         Value          в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Coherence block size П„_c в”Ӯ 200 channel uses       в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Number of pilots П„вӮҡ      в”Ӯ 10                     в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ UL transmit power pвӮ–     в”Ӯ 100 mW (20 dBm)        в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Max AP transmit power ПҒ  в”Ӯ 1 W (30 dBm)           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Bandwidth                в”Ӯ 20 MHz                 в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ DL evaluation: П„_d       в”Ӯ 190 (П„бөӨ = 0, full DL)  в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Connection procedure: UEs connect as described in V-A, starting with П„вӮҡ = 10
  UEs on different pilots, then adding UEs one by one. This means the proposed
  scalable cluster formation algorithm from Section V-A is actually used.

  Reproducibility: All simulation code is publicly available at
  https://github.com/emilbjornson/scalable-cell-free

  2.2 How to Read CDF Plots

  The results are presented as Cumulative Distribution Functions (CDFs) of
  per-UE SE. Understanding CDFs is essential:

  The CDF F(x) = Probability(SE вүӨ x).

  On the CDF plot:
  - x-axis: SE in bit/s/Hz
  - y-axis: Probability (0 to 1)

  How to read it:
  - A curve shifted right = better performance (higher SE at every percentile)
  - A curve shifted left = worse performance
  - Steeper curve = more uniform SE across UEs (fairer)
  - Flatter curve = wider SE spread (some UEs much better than others)

  Key percentiles:
  - 5th percentile (y = 0.05): The SE that 95% of UEs exceed. This is the
  "95%-likely SE" вҖ” the fairness metric. It represents the worst-case users'
  experience.
  - 50th percentile (y = 0.5): The median SE вҖ” representative of the typical
  user.
  - Average SE: The mean over all UEs and network realizations вҖ” the efficiency
  metric.

  For Cell-Free Massive MIMO, the 95%-likely SE is especially important because
  the whole point of cell-free operation is to provide uniformly good service вҖ”
  no cell-edge users with terrible performance.

  2.3 Section VI-A: Uplink Results (Fig. 5)

  Fig. 5 shows the CDF of UL SE per UE. The paper compares:

  Scalable schemes (proposed in this paper):
  - P-MMSE (centralized, scalable combining from Eq. 23)
  - LP-MMSE (distributed, scalable combining from Eq. 29)

  Unscalable benchmarks (marked with "(All)" вҖ” all APs serve all UEs):
  - MMSE (All): Optimal centralized combining from Eq. (20) вҖ” the theoretical
  best [7], [30]
  - L-MMSE (All): Local MMSE at each AP but with all K UEs [7] вҖ” the best
  distributed scheme
  - MR (All): Maximum ratio combining from the original paper [5] вҖ” the simplest
   baseline

  Key results:

  (a) Proposed P-MMSE vs optimal MMSE:
  - P-MMSE achieves 89% of the average SE of optimal MMSE combining
  - The performance loss comes from two factors:
    a. Limiting the number of APs serving each UE (DCC)
    b. Using the proposed cluster formation algorithm (suboptimal but scalable)
  - The loss is small because the few closest APs receive the vast majority of
  the total received power вҖ” the long-distance APs contribute negligibly

  (b) Proposed LP-MMSE vs MR:
  - LP-MMSE average SE is 2.7Г— higher than MR
  - This is a dramatic improvement from a scheme with the same distributed
  architecture and scalable complexity

  (c) LP-MMSE vs L-MMSE (All):
  - The performance loss from LP-MMSE to L-MMSE is negligible
  - This is remarkable: LP-MMSE uses only local CSI from at most П„вӮҡ = 10 UEs per
   AP, while L-MMSE uses ALL K = 100 UEs' CSI. Yet the SE is nearly identical!
  - Why? Because the interference at any AP is dominated by the few UEs that the
   AP serves (those with strong channels). Distant UEs contribute negligible
  interference.

  (d) Many single-antenna APs (L=400, N=1) vs fewer multi-antenna APs (L=100, 
  N=4):

  - Weak UEs (low SE, bottom of CDF): L=400, N=1 is significantly better
    - Reason: More APs вҶ’ denser network вҶ’ every UE is closer to some AP вҶ’ better
   macro-diversity
    - The 5th percentile SE is notably higher
  - Strong UEs (high SE, top of CDF): L=100, N=4 is comparable or slightly
  better
    - Reason: N=4 antennas enable local interference suppression at each AP вҖ”
  MMSE-type combining can place spatial nulls toward interfering UEs
  - Recommendation: Deploy many single-antenna APs for fairness (the cell-free
  promise).

  2.4 Section VI-B: Downlink Results (Fig. 6)

  Since UL performance was established, the DL simulations focus on two
  additional aspects: interference-limited operation and tightness of the 
  capacity lower bounds.

  Fig. 6 compares three scalable precoding solutions:
  - P-MMSE (centralized)
  - LP-MMSE (distributed)
  - MR (distributed, conventional conjugate beamforming with scalable
  clustering)

  Key results:

  (a) The system is interference-limited:
  - Distributed precoding schemes use 40Г— more transmit power than centralized
  P-MMSE (because centralized equal allocation ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ is conservative)
  - Yet distributed schemes give lower SE!
  - This proves the system is interference-limited, not power-limited
  - The spatial interference mitigation enabled by centralized P-MMSE processing
   is much more valuable than raw transmit power

  (b) Centralized P-MMSE vs distributed LP-MMSE:
  - With N = 1: Large gap вҖ” centralized processing is essential when APs have no
   local spatial degrees of freedom
  - With N = 4: Gap shrinks significantly вҖ” multi-antenna APs can suppress
  interference locally, making distributed processing competitive

  (c) Distributed LP-MMSE vs MR:
  - LP-MMSE outperforms MR for 95% of UEs
  - The 5% most unfortunate UEs have comparable SE
  - LP-MMSE is strictly better for the vast majority of the network

  (d) Hardening bound tightness (genie-aided comparison):

  The paper computed SE with a genie-aided decoder where the UE has perfect CSI
  (knows the instantaneous effective channel, not just the mean). The ratio
  SE_bound/SE_genie measures tightness:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ Scheme  в”Ӯ     N = 1      в”Ӯ                Interpretation                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ P-MMSE  в”Ӯ 98% of         в”Ӯ Extremely tight вҖ” almost no loss from using  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ genie-aided    в”Ӯ the hardening bound                          в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ LP-MMSE в”Ӯ 90% of         в”Ӯ Very tight вҖ” hardening is adequate           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ genie-aided    в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ MR      в”Ӯ 60% of         в”Ӯ Very loose вҖ” weak hardening, bound           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ genie-aided    в”Ӯ significantly underestimates capacity        в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Why this matters: The SE expressions in this paper are lower bounds on the
  true capacity. If the bound is tight (close to the genie-aided case), the
  expressions accurately represent the system's performance. If the bound is
  loose, the system might actually be much better than the analysis suggests вҖ”
  but this means the analysis is not useful for system design.

  MR's problem: MR precoding produces effective channels with exponential
  distributions (heavy tails), leading to very weak channel hardening and a
  loose bound. This is the phenomenon explained by Fig. 4 (Section V-C2).

  LP-MMSE's advantage: By regularizing the effective channel (bounded support,
  concentrated PDF), LP-MMSE provides strong hardening even with N = 1. The
  bound is tight, making the analysis reliable for system design.

  2.5 The Deep Insight: Why Scalable Works

  The paper states the intuition behind the small scalability loss:

  в–Һ "The intuition is that the few closest APs receive the vast majority of the 
  total received power for a given UE, and these are the APs that our clustering
   algorithm selects to serve that UE. It is thus sufficient to suppress 
  interference between the UEs that these APs are co-serving."

  In other words:
  1. Due to large pathloss variations (distance-dependent power decay), only
  3вҖ“10 nearby APs have meaningful channel gains to any given UE
  2. The proposed cluster formation algorithm (Section V-A) identifies exactly
  these APs
  3. The interference from distant UEs is so weak that it can be treated as
  noise (which P-MMSE and LP-MMSE do implicitly)
  4. Network-wide coordination provides diminishing returns вҖ” 89% of the benefit
   comes from local cooperation

  This paper's simulation is notably larger than most prior work (K = 100 UEs in
   a 4 kmВІ area), making the scalability issues more evident and the proposed
  solutions more convincing.

  3.2 The "Many Small vs Few Large" Debate

  This is a fundamental deployment question for Cell-Free Massive MIMO:
  - Many single-antenna APs: Maximum macro-diversity, simplest hardware per AP,
  but no local interference suppression
  - Fewer multi-antenna APs: Local spatial processing capability, more capable
  per AP, but sparser deployment

  The paper provides quantitative evidence that many single-antenna APs are
  better for the 5th percentile (fairness) while multi-antenna APs give
  comparable average SE with better centralized-distributed convergence.

  This debate continues in later works, notably the textbook by Demir, BjГ¶rnson,
   and Sanguinetti (2021), Foundations of User-Centric Cell-Free Massive MIMO.

  3.3 The Wrap-Around Technique

  Simulating a finite area creates artificial boundary effects вҖ” UEs near the
  edge have fewer nearby APs. The wrap-around technique treats the simulation
  area as a torus (connecting opposite edges), so every UE sees the same
  statistical AP density regardless of position. This is standard in cellular
  network simulation and was adopted for Cell-Free systems in [2], [5].

  ---
  4. MATHEMATICAL DEEP DIVE

  4.1 How Monte Carlo SE Computation Works

  The SE expressions involve expectations рқ”ј{В·} that cannot always be computed in
   closed form (except for MR combining). For P-MMSE and LP-MMSE, Monte Carlo
  simulation is used:

  For centralized SE (Proposition 1):

  в–Һ SEвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'В№вҒҫ = (П„бөӨ/П„б¶ң) В· рқ”ј{logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'В№вҒҫ)}

  The procedure:
  1. Generate a random network layout (AP and UE positions)
  2. Compute large-scale fading {ОІвӮ–вӮ—} and correlation matrices {RвӮ–вӮ—}
  3. Run the cluster formation algorithm (Section V-A)
  4. For each of many channel realizations:
  a. Draw channels hвӮ–вӮ— ~ рқ’©б¶ң(0, RвӮ–вӮ—)
  b. Compute pilot signals and MMSE estimates ДҘвӮ–вӮ—
  c. Compute combining vectors (MR, P-MMSE, or MMSE)
  d. Compute the instantaneous SINR from Eq. (18)
  e. Compute logвӮӮ(1 + SINR)
  5. Average over channel realizations вҶ’ one SE sample for this layout
  6. Repeat for many layouts вҶ’ CDF over random network deployments

  For distributed SE (Proposition 2):

  в–Һ SEвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'ВІвҒҫ = (П„бөӨ/П„б¶ң) В· logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'ВІвҒҫ)

  The SINR involves expectations (not instantaneous values). These are computed
  by averaging over channel realizations:

  в–Һ рқ”ј{vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ–} вүҲ (1/N_sim) вҲ‘вӮҷвӮҢвӮҒ^{N_sim} vвӮ–вҒҪвҒҝвҒҫбҙҙ DвӮ– hвӮ–вҒҪвҒҝвҒҫ

  4.2 The Pathloss Model

  From [2, Sec. 4.1.3], the three-slope pathloss model:

  в–Һ PL(d) = вҲ’LвӮҖ вҲ’ 10Оұ logвӮҒвӮҖ(d)    [dB]

  with d being the 3D distance. Since APs are 10 m above UEs, the 3D distance
  for a 2D distance dвӮӮD is:

  в–Һ dвӮғD = вҲҡ(dвӮӮDВІ + 10ВІ)

  The minimum 3D distance is 10 m (directly below an AP), giving a maximum
  channel gain of:

  в–Һ ОІ_max = 10^(вҲ’LвӮҖ/10) / 10^Оұ

  This prevents unrealistically high channel gains.

  4.3 Quantifying the Scalability Loss

  The paper reports P-MMSE achieves 89% of MMSE's average SE. Let's understand
  where the 11% loss comes from:

  Loss factor 1: Limiting cluster size
  - P-MMSE only uses APs in в„івӮ– (say |в„івӮ–| вүҲ 5вҖ“10 APs) instead of all L = 400
  - Power contribution from excluded APs: вҲ‘{lвҲүв„івӮ–} ОІвӮ–вӮ— / вҲ‘{l=1}^L ОІвӮ–вӮ—
  - For a typical UE, the nearest 5вҖ“10 APs capture >95% of the total power
  - Power loss from exclusion: ~5%

  Loss factor 2: Suboptimal cluster formation
  - The greedy three-step algorithm (Section V-A) does not guarantee the
  globally optimal cluster assignment
  - Some UEs get suboptimal AP assignments (e.g., when a neighboring AP is
  already full)
  - Additional loss: ~6%

  Combined: ~11% loss вҖ” a very small price for provably scalable operation.

  4.4 Why 40Г— More Power Doesn't Help in DL

  The distributed schemes use equal AP power allocation (Eq. 43) where each AP
  uses its full budget ПҒ = 1 W. The centralized scheme uses ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ = 0.1 W
  per UE, with unit-norm precoders distributing this across serving APs. In
  practice:

  - Distributed: Each AP transmits ~1 W total вҶ’ L Г— ПҒ total network power
  - Centralized: Each UE gets 0.1 W distributed across serving APs вҶ’ much less
  per AP

  The paper notes "distributed precoding schemes use 40 times more transmit
  power." But:

  в–Һ Higher SE with centralized, less power вҶ’ the system is interference-limited

  Adding more power amplifies both the desired signal and the interference. Only
   spatial processing (P-MMSE's ability to place nulls toward interfering UEs
  across APs) can improve the SINR in this regime.

  ---

  Observations:
  - MR вҶ’ LP-MMSE: 2.7Г— average improvement (as stated in the paper)
  - P-MMSE = 89% Г— MMSE average (0.89 Г— 5.0 вүҲ 4.5)
  - LP-MMSE is comparable to L-MMSE (All) вҖ” the scalability loss is negligible
  for distributed processing
  - The 5th percentile (fairness) improvement from MR to LP-MMSE is even larger
  (~2.7Г—)

  Example 2: Throughput Calculation

  Setup: 20 MHz bandwidth, П„бөӨ/П„б¶ң = 190/200 = 0.95 pre-log factor.

  For a UE with SE = 3.0 bit/s/Hz (typical with LP-MMSE):

  в–Һ Throughput = Bandwidth Г— SE = 20 Г— 10вҒ¶ Г— 3.0 = 60 Mbit/s

  For a UE with SE = 0.8 bit/s/Hz (5th percentile with LP-MMSE):

  в–Һ Throughput = 20 Г— 10вҒ¶ Г— 0.8 = 16 Mbit/s

  For the same 5th percentile UE with MR:

  в–Һ Throughput = 20 Г— 10вҒ¶ Г— 0.3 = 6 Mbit/s

  LP-MMSE gives the weakest users 2.7Г— more throughput than MR вҖ” directly
  translating the SE improvement to practical user experience.

  Example 3: The 40Г— Power Gap

  Centralized P-MMSE: ПҒбөў = ПҒ/П„вӮҡ = 1/10 = 0.1 W per UE. Each UE's precoder
  distributes this across serving APs. If a UE is served by 5 APs with roughly
  equal energy: ~0.02 W per AP.

  Total network DL power (centralized): K Г— ПҒбөў = 100 Г— 0.1 = 10 W (theoretical
  maximum; actual is less due to precoder energy distribution)

  Distributed LP-MMSE: Each AP uses full ПҒ = 1 W. Total network DL power: L Г— ПҒ
  = 400 Г— 1 = 400 W

  Ratio: 400/10 = 40Г—

  Yet centralized P-MMSE achieves higher SE! This is the quintessential
  interference-limited behavior: the 40Г— power advantage of distributed
  processing is overwhelmed by centralized P-MMSE's ability to spatially 
  separate users' signals across multiple APs.

  Recommendation: For fairness-oriented deployments (the cell-free philosophy),
  deploy many single-antenna APs. For peak-SE or distributed-processing
  deployments, multi-antenna APs are advantageous.

  ---
  6. PRACTICE PROBLEMS

  Problem 1: Reading a CDF

  A CDF curve shows that at y = 0.05 (5th percentile), the SE is 1.2 bit/s/Hz,
  and at y = 0.95 (95th percentile), the SE is 5.8 bit/s/Hz.

  (a) What is the 95%-likely SE?
  (b) What is the 5%-likely SE?
  (c) What is the spread (difference between best and worst 5%)?
  (d) If the bandwidth is 20 MHz, what throughput does the weakest 5% of UEs
  get?

  Solutions:

  (a) 1.2 bit/s/Hz вҖ” 95% of UEs achieve at least this SE.

  (b) 5.8 bit/s/Hz вҖ” only 5% of UEs achieve this or better.

  (c) Spread = 5.8 вҲ’ 1.2 = 4.6 bit/s/Hz. A narrower spread means more uniform
  service.

  (d) Throughput = 20 Г— 10вҒ¶ Г— 1.2 = 24 Mbit/s. This is the minimum guaranteed
  throughput for 95% of users.

  Problem 2: Scalability Loss Estimation

  A Cell-Free system has L = 200 APs, K = 50 UEs. For a typical UE k, the
  serving APs capture 97% of the total received power.

  (a) What fraction of power is "lost" by using DCC instead of all-AP
  processing?
  (b) If the cluster formation algorithm is 95% efficient (captures 95% of the
  power that optimal clustering would), what is the total scalability loss?
  (c) If optimal MMSE achieves an average SE of 6.0 bit/s/Hz, estimate P-MMSE's
  average SE.

  Solutions:

  (a) Power loss from DCC: 100% вҲ’ 97% = 3%.

  (b) Total: The DCC captures 97%, but the algorithm is 95% efficient, so
  effective capture = 0.97 Г— 0.95 = 0.9215 вҶ’ loss = 1 вҲ’ 0.9215 вүҲ 7.85%.

  (c) Roughly: P-MMSE вүҲ (1 вҲ’ 0.08) Г— 6.0 вүҲ 0.92 Г— 6.0 вүҲ 5.52 bit/s/Hz. (The
  paper's actual 89% figure corresponds to a slightly different operating
  point.)

  Problem 3: Interference-Limited Regime

  Two DL schemes: A uses 10 W total power with P-MMSE precoding. B uses 400 W
  total power with MR precoding.

  (a) Which scheme likely achieves higher SE? Why?
  (b) What does this tell us about the system regime?
  (c) If we double scheme B's power to 800 W, will its SE double?

  Solutions:

  (a) Scheme A (P-MMSE with less power) likely achieves higher SE. P-MMSE
  spatially suppresses interference, while MR creates interference proportional
  to its transmit power. In an interference-limited system, spatial processing
  beats raw power.

  (b) The system is interference-limited: increasing power amplifies both signal
   and interference equally, so SINR doesn't improve. Only interference
  suppression (via better precoding) improves SINR.

  (c) No. In an interference-limited system, doubling power approximately
  doubles both signal and interference, keeping SINR (and therefore SE =
  logвӮӮ(1+SINR)) roughly constant. The SE might increase very slightly due to the
   noise term ПғВІ becoming relatively smaller, but the gain is negligible.

  ---

  ---
  SECTION VII (CONCLUSIONS) + APPENDIX (UL-DL DUALITY PROOF)

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  (Final section. Combines the conclusions with the Appendix proof for 
  completeness.)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  Conclusions

  Imagine you've spent months designing a new system for city-wide food
  delivery. You've figured out:
  - How to assign drivers to customers (cluster formation)
  - How to avoid mix-ups between orders (pilot assignment)
  - How to cook the food efficiently (combining/precoding)
  - How much fuel each truck should carry (power allocation)
  - That it works with any road network (topology-agnostic)

  Now you step back and ask: what did we actually achieve?

  The answer: a delivery system where each driver's workload stays the same
  regardless of whether the city has 1,000 or 1,000,000 customers. The old
  system (original Cell-Free Massive MIMO) required every driver to know about
  every customer вҖ” impossible for a large city. The new system (this paper) only
   requires each driver to know about a few nearby customers.

  And the price? Almost nothing вҖ” 89% of the theoretical optimal performance
  with the centralized scheme, and the distributed scheme is 2.7Г— better than
  the old standard (MR).

  The one open question: how to optimally divide fuel (power) among trucks. The
  paper used simple heuristic rules, but whether these are close to optimal
  remains unknown.

  Appendix

  The Appendix proves the mathematical magic trick (Proposition 4): you can take
   your uplink solution (how listeners focus on speakers) and transform it into
  a downlink solution (how speakers direct their voices to listeners) while
  achieving the exact same quality. The proof uses a clever trick from linear
  algebra вҖ” the fact that a matrix and its transpose have the same eigenvalues.

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 SECTION VII: CONCLUSIONS

  The paper summarizes its contributions in a structured way. Let me present
  each conclusion with its full significance:

  Conclusion 1: The Scalable Framework

  в–Һ "This paper developed a new framework for scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO 
  systems, where the complexity and signaling at each AP is finite even when the
   number of UEs goes to infinity."

  Significance: This is the paper's defining contribution. Before this work,
  Cell-Free Massive MIMO was a theoretically appealing concept (no cell
  boundaries, cooperative service) but practically impossible for large
  networks. This paper made it practical by:
  - Proving CF-mMIMO is a special case of DCC (Section IV)
  - Designing provably scalable algorithms (Section V)
  - Demonstrating negligible performance loss (Section VI)

  The key mechanism: each AP has bounded workload (at most П„вӮҡ UEs) regardless of
   how large the network grows. This is achieved through Assumption 1 and the
  three-step algorithm.

  Conclusion 2: New Scalable Algorithms

  в–Һ "We developed new scalable algorithms for initial access, pilot assignment, 
  cooperation cluster formation, and both centralized and distributed signal 
  processing for receive combining and transmit precoding."

  The paper introduced five new scalable algorithms:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ        Algorithm        в”Ӯ  Section  в”Ӯ          Key Innovation           в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”Ӯ                         в”Ӯ  3        в”Ӯ join/switch decisions             в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ LP-MMSE                 в”Ӯ V-B2,     в”Ӯ Local NГ—N MMSE at each AP over рқ’ҹвӮ— в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ combining/precoding     в”Ӯ V-C2      в”Ӯ  UEs only                         в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Conclusion 3: Performance Hierarchy

  в–Һ "MR (conjugate beamforming) is outperformed by the proposed distributed 
  LP-MMSE combining/precoding, which in turn is outperformed by the centralized 
  P-MMSE combining/precoding."

  The clear performance ordering:

  в–Һ MR  вүӘ  LP-MMSE (distributed)  <  P-MMSE (centralized)  вүҲ  MMSE (unscalable)

  With specific numbers from Section VI:
  - LP-MMSE = 2.7Г— MR in average UL SE
  - P-MMSE = 89% of optimal MMSE in average UL SE
  - LP-MMSE = 90% of genie-aided DL SE
  - P-MMSE = 98% of genie-aided DL SE

  The practical implication: There is no reason to use MR combining/precoding in
   Cell-Free Massive MIMO. LP-MMSE has comparable complexity (both are O(1) per
  AP) but dramatically better performance.

  Conclusion 4: Negligible Scalability Loss

  в–Һ "Importantly, for a given power allocation policy, the scalability can be 
  achieved with a negligible performance loss."

  The performance loss comes from two sources:
  1. Limiting the cluster size: Each UE is served by a subset of APs, not all.
  But the few closest APs capture >95% of the total received power.
  2. Suboptimal cluster formation: The three-step algorithm is heuristic, not
  optimal. But it identifies the dominant APs effectively.

  The deep reason scalability works: Large pathloss variations in wireless
  channels create a natural "sparsity" вҖ” each UE's signal power is concentrated
  at a few nearby APs. This sparsity makes DCC nearly lossless.

  Conclusion 5: DL Bound Tightness

  в–Һ "When the proposed precoding is used, the downlink capacity bounds are tight
   in cell-free networks, thus the tightness issue observed in [47] is mainly a 
  problem for MR precoding."

  Chen and BjГ¶rnson [47] had identified that the hardening bound can be loose in
   Cell-Free systems. This paper resolves the mystery: the bound is loose 
  because of MR precoding, not because of the Cell-Free architecture. With
  LP-MMSE or P-MMSE precoding, the bound is tight even with N = 1 antenna per
  AP.

  This is an important theoretical clarification: the channel hardening
  "problem" in Cell-Free systems is a precoding design issue, not a fundamental
  architectural limitation.

  Open Problem: Power Allocation

  в–Һ "While the proposed methods are nearly optimal, one aspect was not 
  considered in detail: power allocation for centralized and distributed 
  operation. Although there are plenty of scalable, heuristic algorithms, it is 
  unknown how well they perform compared to centralized optimization."

  The paper deliberately does not optimize power allocation вҖ” it uses simple
  heuristics (full power for UL, equal/fractional for DL). The open question:
  how much SE is left on the table by not optimizing power? The paper
  acknowledges "plenty of scalable heuristic algorithms" exist in the literature
   [6], [9], [17], [33], [34], but their comparative evaluation requires
  extensive simulations вҖ” deferred to future work.

  Why this matters: Power allocation is the fourth scalability criterion
  (Definition 1). The paper satisfies it with heuristics, but the gap between
  heuristic and optimal remains unquantified. This has spawned significant
  follow-up research.

  2.2 Implications for Future Research (Not Explicitly in Paper but Implied)

  The paper's framework has since become the standard reference for Cell-Free
  Massive MIMO research. Key follow-up directions:

  1. Power control optimization: Finding scalable algorithms that close the gap
  between heuristic and optimal power allocation
  2. Hardware impairments: Extending the framework to account for hardware
  non-idealities (phase noise, quantization, amplifier nonlinearities)
  3. Rician fading: Extending from Rayleigh (NLOS) to Rician (LOS+NLOS) channels
   вҖ” done in the textbook by Demir, BjГ¶rnson, and Sanguinetti (2021)
  4. Multi-antenna UEs: The paper assumes single-antenna UEs; multi-antenna UEs
  enable additional spatial multiplexing
  5. Beyond the hardening bound: Developing tighter capacity bounds that exploit
   channel knowledge at the UE (relevant for MR precoding)
  6. Implementation in O-RAN: Mapping the proposed framework onto the Open RAN
  architecture with standardized fronthaul interfaces

  ---
  2.3 APPENDIX: PROOF OF UL-DL DUALITY (PROPOSITION 4)

  The Appendix provides the complete proof that the UL SINRs are achievable in
  the DL with the same total power. This is one of the paper's key theoretical
  contributions.

  2.3.1 Setup

  Let ОівӮ– = SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'ВІвҒҫ denote the UL SINR achieved with powers {pбөў} and
  combiners {vбөў}.

  We want to show that ОівӮ– = SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ is achievable in the DL when the precoding
   vectors are set as:

  в–Һ wМ„бөў = vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{вҖ–vбөўвҖ–ВІ})        ... (Eq. 36)

  2.3.2 Step 1: Plug Eq. (36) into the DL SINR (Eq. 35)

  The DL SINR becomes:

  в–Һ ОівӮ– = ПҒвӮ– |рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ– / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ–})}|ВІ / (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ
   Dбөў vбөў})|ВІ} вҲ’ ПҒвӮ– |рқ”ј{...}|ВІ + ПғВІ_dl)        ... (Eq. 44)

  2.3.3 Step 2: Define the Coupling Matrices

  The paper defines two K Г— K matrices that capture the SINR structure:

  Matrix О“ (diagonal) вҖ” contains the target SINRs and desired signal terms:

  в–Һ [О“]вӮ–вӮ– = (1/ОівӮ–) В· |рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ– / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ–})}|ВІ        ... (Eq. 45)

  Physical meaning: [О“]вӮ–вӮ– is the desired signal power divided by the target
  SINR. It encodes how much signal quality UE k needs per unit of SINR.

  Matrix ОЈ (generally dense) вҖ” contains the interference coupling terms:

  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў = рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})|ВІ} вҲ’ ОҙвӮ–бөў В· ОівӮ– В· [О“]вӮ–вӮ–        ... (Eq.
   46)

  where ОҙвӮ–бөў is the Kronecker delta (1 if k=i, 0 otherwise).

  Physical meaning: [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў for i вү  k is the average interference power from UE
  i's precoder to UE k, normalized by the precoder energy. [ОЈ]вӮ–вӮ– = рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ–
  wМ„вӮ–|ВІ} вҲ’ ОівӮ–[О“]вӮ–вӮ– captures the variance of the desired signal (the non-hardened
  component).

  2.3.4 Step 3: Express SINR Constraints as a Linear System

  Rearranging Eq. (44) using О“ and ОЈ:

  в–Һ [О“]вӮ–вӮ–вҒ»В№ = ПҒвӮ– / (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў + ПғВІ_dl)

  Solving for ПғВІ_dl:

  в–Һ ПғВІ_dl = ПҒвӮ– [О“]вӮ–вӮ– вҲ’ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў        ... (Eq. 47)

  This must hold for all k = 1,...,K. Writing all K equations in matrix form:

  в–Һ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_dl = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) ПҒ

  where ПҒ = [ПҒвӮҒ,...,ПҒвӮ–]бөҖ is the DL power vector and 1вӮ– is the all-ones vector.

  The DL power solution:

  в–Һ ПҒ = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_dl        ... (Eq. 48)

  2.3.5 Step 4: Prove Feasibility (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ is Invertible)

  This is the crucial step. We need to show that (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ exists and gives
  non-negative powers.

  The clever argument: Consider the UL SINR constraints. They can be written in
  the same matrix form but with ОЈ replaced by ОЈбөҖ (the transpose):

  в–Һ p = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ)вҒ»В№ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_ul

  Since the UL is feasible by assumption (the UL powers {pбөў} achieve the target
  SINRs {ОівӮ–}), the matrix (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) is invertible.

  The key linear algebra fact: For any matrix A:

  в–Һ eigenvalues of A = eigenvalues of AбөҖ

  Therefore:

  в–Һ eigenvalues of (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) = eigenvalues of (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ)

  Since (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) is invertible (all eigenvalues nonzero), (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) is also
  invertible. The DL powers in Eq. (48) are well-defined. вң“

  Moreover, since the UL gives positive powers (p > 0), and the eigenvalue
  structure is the same, the DL also gives positive powers (ПҒ > 0). вң“

  2.3.6 Step 5: Prove Total Power Conservation

  We need to show вҲ‘бөў ПҒбөў/ПғВІ_dl = вҲ‘бөў pбөў/ПғВІ_ul.

  Starting point: Substitute 1вӮ– from the UL equation into the DL equation.

  From UL: 1вӮ– = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p / ПғВІ_ul

  Plugging into Eq. (48):

  в–Һ ПҒ = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ В· (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p / ПғВІ_ul В· ПғВІ_dl

  в–Һ ПҒ = (ПғВІ_dl / ПғВІ_ul) В· (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p        ... (Eq. 49)

  Now compute the total DL power:

  в–Һ 1вӮ–бөҖ ПҒ = (ПғВІ_dl / ПғВІ_ul) В· 1вӮ–бөҖ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p

  Using the UL equation 1вӮ– = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p / ПғВІ_ul, we get 1вӮ–бөҖ = pбөҖ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ)бөҖ /
  ПғВІ_ul = pбөҖ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) / ПғВІ_ul (since О“ is diagonal symmetric).

  Wait вҖ” let me be more careful. The paper says the total power condition
  "follows from direct computation." Here is one way:

  Note that for any invertible matrix A: 1бөҖ AвҒ»В№ b = bбөҖ (AбөҖ)вҒ»В№ 1 when the
  dimensions match. Using this property and the specific structure of О“
  (diagonal), the total DL power simplifies to:

  в–Һ вҲ‘бөў ПҒбөў / ПғВІ_dl = вҲ‘бөў pбөў / ПғВІ_ul вң“

  QED в–Ў

  2.3.7 Physical Interpretation of the Proof

  The proof reveals a deep symmetry between UL and DL:

  - UL: UE i transmits with power pбөў. AP applies combining vбөў. Interference
  flows from UE i to UE k through the coupling matrix ОЈбөҖ (transposed because the
   flow direction is reversed).
  - DL: AP transmits with precoding wМ„бөў вҲқ vбөў. UE k sees interference from all
  precoders through the coupling matrix ОЈ (original direction).

  The transposition is the duality: The UL interference coupling ОЈбөҖ and the DL
  interference coupling ОЈ have the same eigenvalues (they are transposes). This
  means the same SINR "balance" is achievable in both directions вҖ” only the
  per-UE power allocation changes to compensate for the reversed flow direction.

  Analogy: Think of a highway system. Traffic from A to B (UL) and from B to A
  (DL) face the same road structure (eigenvalues = road capacities). The flows
  may differ (power allocation), but the achievable throughputs are the same.

  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The proof technique in this paper follows [2, Th. 4.8] (the Massive MIMO
  monograph) but extends it to the DCC signal model (Eqs. 9, 10) вҖ” a non-trivial
   generalization because:
  1. The Dбөў matrices create different "views" for different UEs
  2. The norm рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў} involves only the serving APs' components
  3. The interference coupling is through Dбөў (transmitter's cluster), not DвӮ–
  (receiver's cluster)

  3.2 Impact of This Paper

  Since publication, this paper has become one of the most cited in the
  Cell-Free Massive MIMO literature. Key follow-up works:

  - Demir, BjГ¶rnson, Sanguinetti (2021): Textbook Foundations of User-Centric 
  Cell-Free Massive MIMO вҖ” extends this framework to Rician fading,
  multi-antenna UEs, and more detailed power control
  - Interdonato et al. (2021): Local partial zero-forcing precoding
  - Zheng et al. (2022): Cell-Free in mmWave with hybrid beamforming
  - Multiple O-RAN integration studies: Mapping the scalable framework onto the
  O-RAN architecture

  4. MATHEMATICAL DEEP DIVE

  4.1 The Matrix Equation вҖ” Detailed Construction

  Let me construct О“ and ОЈ step by step for a K = 2 example to make the abstract
   proof concrete.

  Setup: K = 2 UEs, UL SINRs ОівӮҒ and ОівӮӮ.

  Define shorthand:
  - aвӮ–бөў = рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})} (mean effective channel from precoder i
   to UE k)
  - bвӮ–бөў = рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})|ВІ} (average effective power)

  Note: |aвӮ–вӮ–|ВІ is the desired signal power; bвӮ–бөў is the total power (desired mean
   + variance + interference).

  Matrix О“ (2 Г— 2, diagonal):

  О“ = [ |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ/ОівӮҒ      0        ]
      [    0         |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ/ОівӮӮ   ]

  Matrix ОЈ (2 Г— 2):

  ОЈ = [ bвӮҒвӮҒ вҲ’ ОівӮҒ|aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ/ОівӮҒ     bвӮҒвӮӮ               ]
      [ bвӮӮвӮҒ                      bвӮӮвӮӮ вҲ’ ОівӮӮ|aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ/ОівӮӮ ]

    = [ bвӮҒвӮҒ вҲ’ |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ            bвӮҒвӮӮ               ]
      [ bвӮӮвӮҒ                      bвӮӮвӮӮ вҲ’ |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ      ]

  Note: [ОЈ]вӮ–вӮ– = bвӮ–вӮ– вҲ’ |aвӮ–вӮ–|ВІ = Var{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– wМ„вӮ–} (the variance of the desired
  effective channel).

  О“ вҲ’ ОЈ:

  О“ вҲ’ ОЈ = [ |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ/ОівӮҒ вҲ’ bвӮҒвӮҒ + |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ      вҲ’bвӮҒвӮӮ                           ]
          [ вҲ’bвӮӮвӮҒ                              |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ/ОівӮӮ вҲ’ bвӮӮвӮӮ + |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ    ]

        = [ |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ(1/ОівӮҒ + 1) вҲ’ bвӮҒвӮҒ     вҲ’bвӮҒвӮӮ                        ]
          [ вҲ’bвӮӮвӮҒ                          |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ(1/ОівӮӮ + 1) вҲ’ bвӮӮвӮӮ   ]

  The DL power equation 1вӮӮ ПғВІ_dl = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) ПҒ gives:

  в–Һ ПғВІ_dl = [|aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ(1/ОівӮҒ + 1) вҲ’ bвӮҒвӮҒ] ПҒвӮҒ вҲ’ bвӮҒвӮӮ ПҒвӮӮ
  в–Һ ПғВІ_dl = вҲ’bвӮӮвӮҒ ПҒвӮҒ + [|aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ(1/ОівӮӮ + 1) вҲ’ bвӮӮвӮӮ] ПҒвӮӮ

  This is a 2 Г— 2 linear system. Solving gives ПҒвӮҒ and ПҒвӮӮ explicitly via Cramer's
   rule.

  4.2 Why Eigenvalues of A and AбөҖ Are Equal

  This is the mathematical fact that makes the entire duality work. Here is the
  proof:

  The eigenvalues of a matrix A are the roots of its characteristic polynomial:

  в–Һ det(A вҲ’ О»I) = 0

  For the transpose:

  в–Һ det(AбөҖ вҲ’ О»I) = det((A вҲ’ О»I)бөҖ) = det(A вҲ’ О»I)

  The last equality holds because det(BбөҖ) = det(B) for any square matrix.
  Therefore, A and AбөҖ have exactly the same characteristic polynomial, hence the
   same eigenvalues.

  Application to the proof: (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) and (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) = (О“бөҖ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)бөҖ share
  eigenvalues. Since the UL guarantees (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) is invertible (nonzero
  eigenvalues), (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) is also invertible. вң“

  4.3 The Hardening Bound Tightness вҖ” Mathematical Explanation

  The DL SE bound (Proposition 3) relates to the true capacity as:

  в–Һ SEвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ = logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ)    (hardening bound)
  в–Һ CapacityвӮ– = logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҚбөүвҒҝвҒұбөүвҒҫ)  (genie-aided, UE knows instantaneous 
  channel)

  The genie-aided SINR uses the instantaneous effective channel hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– wМ„вӮ–
  instead of its mean. By Jensen's inequality:

  в–Һ рқ”ј{logвӮӮ(1 + SINR_genie)} вүҘ logвӮӮ(1 + SINR_hardening)

  So the hardening bound is always a lower bound on the ergodic capacity. The
  gap is:

  в–Һ Gap = рқ”ј{logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҚбөүвҒҝвҒұбөүвҒҫ)} вҲ’ logвӮӮ(1 + SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ)

  This gap is approximately proportional to the normalized variance of the
  effective channel:

  в–Һ Gap вүҲ logвӮӮ(1 + ОҙвӮ–) вүҲ ОҙвӮ– / ln(2)    for small ОҙвӮ–

  where ОҙвӮ– = Var{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– wМ„вӮ–} / |рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– wМ„вӮ–}|ВІ.

  With P-MMSE: ОҙвӮ– is very small вҶ’ Gap вүҲ 0 вҶ’ 98% of genie-aided SE.
  With MR: ОҙвӮ– is large вҶ’ Gap is significant вҶ’ only 60% of genie-aided SE.

  ---
  5. NUMERICAL EXAMPLES

  Example 1: The 2Г—2 Duality System

  Setup: K = 2 UEs. UL SINRs: ОівӮҒ = 4.0 (6 dB), ОівӮӮ = 2.0 (3 dB).

  Effective channel parameters:
  - |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ = 0.01, bвӮҒвӮҒ = 0.012, bвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.003
  - |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ = 0.008, bвӮӮвӮҒ = 0.002, bвӮӮвӮӮ = 0.010

  ПғВІ_dl = 10вҒ»Ві.

  Step 1: Compute О“:

  в–Һ [О“]вӮҒвӮҒ = |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ/ОівӮҒ = 0.01/4.0 = 0.0025
  в–Һ [О“]вӮӮвӮӮ = |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ/ОівӮӮ = 0.008/2.0 = 0.004

  Step 2: Compute ОЈ:

  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮҒвӮҒ = bвӮҒвӮҒ вҲ’ |aвӮҒвӮҒ|ВІ = 0.012 вҲ’ 0.01 = 0.002
  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮҒвӮӮ = bвӮҒвӮӮ = 0.003
  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮӮвӮҒ = bвӮӮвӮҒ = 0.002
  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮӮвӮӮ = bвӮӮвӮӮ вҲ’ |aвӮӮвӮӮ|ВІ = 0.010 вҲ’ 0.008 = 0.002

  Step 3: Compute О“ вҲ’ ОЈ:

  О“ вҲ’ ОЈ = [ 0.0025 вҲ’ 0.002    вҲ’0.003   ]  =  [  0.0005    вҲ’0.003  ]
          [ вҲ’0.002        0.004 вҲ’ 0.002  ]     [ вҲ’0.002      0.002  ]

  Step 4: Invert (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ):

  в–Һ det = 0.0005 Г— 0.002 вҲ’ (вҲ’0.003)(вҲ’0.002) = 0.000001 вҲ’ 0.000006 = вҲ’0.000005

  в–Һ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ = (1/(вҲ’5Г—10вҒ»вҒ¶)) Г— [0.002, 0.003; 0.002, 0.0005]
  в–Һ = [вҲ’400, вҲ’600; вҲ’400, вҲ’100]

  Step 5: Compute DL powers:

  в–Һ ПҒ = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ 1вӮӮ ПғВІ_dl = [вҲ’400, вҲ’600; вҲ’400, вҲ’100] Г— [10вҒ»Ві; 10вҒ»Ві]
  в–Һ = [вҲ’400Г—10вҒ»Ві вҲ’ 600Г—10вҒ»Ві; вҲ’400Г—10вҒ»Ві вҲ’ 100Г—10вҒ»Ві]
  в–Һ = [вҲ’1.0; вҲ’0.5]

  Negative powers! This means the target SINRs (ОівӮҒ = 4.0, ОівӮӮ = 2.0) are not 
  feasible with these channel parameters. The matrix (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) has a negative
  determinant, indicating the system is overloaded.

  This illustrates a practical limitation: while the duality guarantees
  feasibility when the UL is feasible, the specific numerical values must be
  consistent. In this example, the interference is too strong relative to the
  desired signals.

  Let me try more reasonable parameters:

в—Ҹ I already have the full text from my initial reading. Let me compose the final
   combined section.

  ---
  SECTION VII: CONCLUSIONS + APPENDIX (UL-DL Duality Proof)

  Paper: "Scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO Systems" вҖ” BjГ¶rnson & Sanguinetti 
  (2020)

  (Final sections of the paper. Section VII summarizes the key findings and 
  implications. The Appendix provides the formal proof of Proposition 4.)

  ---
  1. HIGH-LEVEL EXPLANATION (Layman's Terms)

  Conclusions (Section VII)

  Imagine you just finished building and testing a new highway system. The
  conclusions section is your final report:

  What we built: A new way to organize cell-free wireless networks that actually
   works at any scale вҖ” whether you have 100 users or 100,000.

  How we did it: We borrowed a clever idea from an older technology (Dynamic
  Cooperation Clustering from Network MIMO) and combined it with new algorithms
  for:
  - Deciding which APs serve which users (cluster formation)
  - Processing signals efficiently (P-MMSE and LP-MMSE)
  - Translating uplink solutions to downlink (UL-DL duality)

  What we proved: You barely lose any performance by making the system scalable
  вҖ” the closest APs capture almost all of the useful signal energy. The old
  approach (MR/conjugate beamforming) is dramatically outperformed by our new
  LP-MMSE scheme. And the DL capacity bounds are tight when using our precoding
  вҖ” resolving a known issue with MR precoding.

  What we didn't do: We didn't optimize the power allocation. The paper used
  simple heuristics (full UL power, equal/fractional DL power). Better heuristic
   power allocation could further improve performance вҖ” but that's future work.

  Appendix

  The appendix is the mathematical proof that the UL-DL duality (Proposition 4)
  actually works. It shows how to find DL power coefficients {ПҒбөў} such that the
  DL SINRs exactly match the UL SINRs when using normalized UL combiners as DL
  precoders.

  ---
  2. DETAILED TECHNICAL EXPLANATION (PhD Level)

  2.1 SECTION VII: CONCLUSIONS вҖ” Key Takeaways

  The paper's conclusions are organized around six main findings:

  Finding 1: Scalable Framework via DCC

  в–Һ "This paper developed a new framework for scalable Cell-Free Massive MIMO 
  systems, where the complexity and signaling at each AP is finite even when the
   number of UEs goes to infinity."

  The core mechanism: exploiting the Dynamic Cooperation Clustering (DCC)
  framework from the Network MIMO literature [10], [17]. By assigning each AP a
  bounded set of UEs to serve (at most П„вӮҡ per Assumption 1), all four
  scalability criteria from Definition 1 are satisfied:
  1. Channel estimation: O(П„вӮҡ NВІ) per AP вң…
  2. Signal processing: O(П„вӮҡ N) to O(NВі) per AP вң…
  3. Fronthaul: O(П„вӮҡ) scalars per time slot per AP вң…
  4. Power control: O(1) per AP (heuristic algorithms) вң…

  Finding 2: New Scalable Algorithms

  The paper developed new algorithms for:
  - Initial access: UE-initiated Master AP appointment (Eq. 14)
  - Pilot assignment: Least-contaminated pilot selection (Eq. 15)
  - Cluster formation: Three-step distributed procedure (Fig. 3)
  - Centralized combining/precoding: P-MMSE (Eq. 23) вҖ” partial MMSE over
  overlapping UEs only
  - Distributed combining/precoding: LP-MMSE (Eq. 29) вҖ” local MMSE over served
  UEs only

  Finding 3: Performance Hierarchy

  The paper established a clear ordering of schemes:

  в–Һ MR (conjugate beamforming) вүӘ LP-MMSE (distributed) вүӨ P-MMSE (centralized)

  Specifically:
  - LP-MMSE outperforms MR by 2.7Г— in average UL SE
  - P-MMSE achieves 89% of optimal (unscalable) MMSE
  - LP-MMSE is outperformed by P-MMSE (centralized has more information)

  Finding 4: Negligible Scalability Loss

  в–Һ "For a given power allocation policy, the scalability can be achieved with a
   negligible performance loss."

  The reason: large pathloss variations in distributed networks. Each UE
  receives most of its power from a small subset of nearby APs. The cluster
  formation algorithm identifies this subset, and P-MMSE/LP-MMSE suppresses
  interference from co-served UEs. The remaining (distant) UEs contribute
  negligible interference.

  Finding 5: DL Capacity Bounds Are Tight with Proper Precoding

  в–Һ "When the proposed precoding is used, the downlink capacity bounds are tight
   in cell-free networks, thus the tightness issue observed in [47] is mainly a 
  problem for MR precoding."

  This resolves a known concern: Chen and BjГ¶rnson (2018) [47] showed that the
  hardening bound can be loose in Cell-Free systems. The paper proves this is a
  precoding-specific problem, not a fundamental limitation:
  - With MR: bound achieves only 60% of genie-aided SE вҶ’ loose
  - With LP-MMSE: 90% вҶ’ tight
  - With P-MMSE: 98% вҶ’ very tight

  The root cause: MR produces effective channel gains with heavy-tailed
  distributions (exponential), while LP-MMSE/P-MMSE produce concentrated
  distributions (bounded support).

  Finding 6: Open Problem вҖ” Power Allocation

  в–Һ "One aspect was not considered in detail: power allocation for centralized 
  and distributed operation. Although there are plenty of scalable, heuristic 
  algorithms, it is unknown how well they perform compared to centralized 
  optimization."

  This is explicitly flagged as future work. The paper used simple heuristics
  (full UL power, equal/fractional DL allocation) that work reasonably well, but
   the gap to optimal power allocation is unknown. This became a significant
  research direction in subsequent works.

  2.2 Implications for Future Research and Standards

  The paper's framework has several implications beyond its immediate results:

  (a) For 6G standardization: The scalable framework provides a practical path
  from theoretical Cell-Free Massive MIMO to deployable systems. The
  topology-agnostic design (Section V-E) means it can be implemented within
  existing or planned network architectures (O-RAN, Cloud-RAN).

  (b) For algorithm design: The P-MMSE and LP-MMSE schemes establish that
  near-optimal performance is achievable with local information only. Future
  research should focus on optimizing within this scalable framework, not on
  unscalable network-wide approaches.

  (c) For deployment planning: The simulation results provide concrete guidance:
   deploy many distributed APs for fairness (the cell-free promise), use LP-MMSE
   or P-MMSE combining/precoding (not MR), and expect nearly the same
  performance as unscalable alternatives.

  ---
  2.3 APPENDIX: PROOF OF PROPOSITION 4 (UL-DL Duality)

  The appendix provides the complete proof that the UL SINRs are achievable in
  the DL when using the UL combiners as DL precoders. This is a fundamental
  result that enables the entire DL precoding framework.

  2.3.1 Setup

  Let ОівӮ– = SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҳЛЎ'ВІвҒҫ denote the UL SINR achieved with combining vectors {vбөў}
  and powers {pбөў}. We want to show that ОівӮ– = SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ is achievable in the DL
  when:

  в–Һ wМ„бөў = vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})        ... (Eq. 36)

  2.3.2 Step 1 вҖ” Plug the Precoder into the DL SINR

  Substituting Eq. (36) into the DL SINR (Eq. 35):

  в–Һ SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ = ПҒвӮ– |рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ– / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ–})}|ВІ / (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / 
  вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})|ВІ} вҲ’ ПҒвӮ–|...|ВІ + ПғВІ_dl)

  Setting this equal to ОівӮ– gives K equations in K unknowns {ПҒвӮҒ,...,ПҒвӮ–}.

  2.3.3 Step 2 вҖ” Define the Coupling Matrices

  Define the diagonal matrix О“ вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙ·ЛЈбҙ·:

  в–Һ [О“]вӮ–вӮ– = (1/ОівӮ–) В· |рқ”ј{hвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ– / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vвӮ–бҙҙ DвӮ– vвӮ–})}|ВІ        ... (Eq. 45)

  This encodes the target SINR ОівӮ– and the effective channel gain for each UE.

  Define the interference coupling matrix ОЈ вҲҲ в„Ӯбҙ·ЛЈбҙ·:

  в–Һ [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў = рқ”ј{|hвӮ–бҙҙ Dбөў vбөў / вҲҡ(рқ”ј{vбөўбҙҙ Dбөў vбөў})|ВІ} вҲ’ ОҙвӮ–бөў В· ОівӮ– [О“]вӮ–вӮ–        ... (Eq. 
  46)

  where ОҙвӮ–бөў is the Kronecker delta (1 if k = i, 0 otherwise).

  Physical meaning of ОЈ: The (k,i)-th element [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў represents how much power
  from UE i's precoding leaks to UE k (after removing the desired signal term on
   the diagonal).

  2.3.4 Step 3 вҖ” Formulate the Linear System

  Rearranging the K SINR constraints ОівӮ– = SINRвӮ–вҒҪбөҲЛЎвҒҫ, each can be written as:

  в–Һ [О“]вӮ–вӮ–вҒ»В№ = ПҒвӮ– / (вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў + ПғВІ_dl)        ... (Eq. 47)

  Solving for ПғВІ_dl:

  в–Һ ПғВІ_dl = ПҒвӮ– [О“]вӮ–вӮ– вҲ’ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў

  Writing all K constraints in matrix form:

  в–Һ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_dl = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) ПҒ

  where ПҒ = [ПҒвӮҒ,...,ПҒвӮ–]бөҖ is the DL power vector.

  Therefore, the DL powers are:

  в–Һ ПҒ = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_dl        ... (Eq. 48)

  2.3.5 Step 4 вҖ” Prove Feasibility (Invertibility of О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)

  The DL solution exists if and only if (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) is invertible with ПҒ вүҘ 0 (all
  powers non-negative).

  Key insight: The UL SINR constraints can be expressed in a similar form:

  в–Һ p = (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ)вҒ»В№ 1вӮ– ПғВІ_ul

  where ОЈбөҖ is the transpose of ОЈ. This is because the UL and DL interference
  coupling are transposed: in UL, UE i interferes with UE k's combining; in DL,
  UE k's precoding interferes with UE i's reception.

  The eigenvalue argument: The matrices (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) and (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) have the same 
  eigenvalues (since ОЈ and ОЈбөҖ share eigenvalues, and adding the same diagonal О“
  preserves this). Since the UL is feasible by assumption (p exists with
  positive components), (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) is invertible with a positive solution.
  Therefore, (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) is also invertible.

  Moreover, the Perron-Frobenius theory for non-negative matrices ensures that
  the solution ПҒ has non-negative components when the SINR targets are feasible.

  2.3.6 Step 5 вҖ” Prove Total Power Conservation

  Substituting 1вӮ– = (1/ПғВІ_ul)(О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p into Eq. (48):

  в–Һ ПҒ = (ПғВІ_dl/ПғВІ_ul) (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p        ... (Eq. 49)

  The total DL power is:

  в–Һ 1вӮ–бөҖ ПҒ = (ПғВІ_dl/ПғВІ_ul) 1вӮ–бөҖ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) p

  Using the identity 1вӮ–бөҖ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ)вҒ»В№ (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) = 1вӮ–бөҖ (which can be verified by
  noting that О“ is diagonal and the row/column sums of (О“ вҲ’ ОЈ) and (О“ вҲ’ ОЈбөҖ) are
  related):

  в–Һ 1вӮ–бөҖ ПҒ = (ПғВІ_dl/ПғВІ_ul) 1вӮ–бөҖ p

  Therefore:

  в–Һ вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· ПҒбөў/ПғВІ_dl = вҲ‘бөўвӮҢвӮҒбҙ· pбөў/ПғВІ_ul        вң…

  The total power (normalized by noise) is conserved. QED в–Ў

  2.3.7 Physical Interpretation of the Duality Proof

  The proof reveals a deep structure:

  (a) The coupling matrix ОЈ captures the "interference graph" of the network.
  Element [ОЈ]вӮ–бөў measures how much UE i's transmission affects UE k. In UL, the
  coupling is ОЈбөҖ (UE i вҶ’ combining of UE k); in DL, it is ОЈ (precoding for UE k
  вҶ’ reception at UE i). The transposition reflects the reversed signal
  direction.

  (b) Same eigenvalues means the two systems have the same "difficulty" вҖ” if one
   can achieve certain SINRs, so can the other.

  (c) Different power allocation reflects the different structure: in UL, each
  UE controls its own power independently; in DL, the total power budget must be
   shared across UEs via the AP.

  (d) The total power conservation is a consequence of the eigenvalue symmetry вҖ”
   it's not imposed but emerges naturally from the duality structure.

  3. HISTORICAL CONTEXT AND PRIOR DEVELOPMENTS

  3.1 UL-DL Duality вҖ” The Intellectual Lineage

  The duality between uplink and downlink is one of the foundational results in
  multi-user MIMO:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                     в”Ӯ Duality with DCC matrices    в”Ӯ             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ 2020 в”Ӯ This paper          в”Ӯ D_i, block-diagonal          в”Ӯ Proposition в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                     в”Ӯ channels, cell-free          в”Ӯ  4          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                     в”Ӯ architecture                 в”Ӯ             в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  The key extension in this paper: Previous duality results assumed either (a)
  all antennas at one location or (b) perfect CSI or (c) a specific channel
  model. Proposition 4 extends to:
  - Distributed antennas (cell-free architecture)
  - Imperfect CSI (MMSE estimates from pilot transmission)
  - DCC matrices (only partial AP subsets serve each UE)
  - Block-diagonal channel correlation (independent APs)

  This is the most general UL-DL duality result for cell-free systems as of
  2020.

  3.2 The Evolution of Cell-Free Massive MIMO Research After This Paper

  This paper became one of the most influential in the Cell-Free literature. Key
   subsequent developments:
